Why Unique Knowledge Is Not a Miracle
Answer to the fourth objection that unique knowledge is miraculous

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the uniqueness of a person's knowledge of a specific drug does not qualify as a miracle according to the author's reasoning.

Core Idea
What is common cannot be miraculous.

The fourth objection claims that the Prophet's unique knowledge of a medicinal remedy would itself be a miracle. In this passage, the author refutes this by pointing out that in every age there are individuals who know things others do not—this is a normal occurrence, not something extraordinary. Therefore, such unique knowledge cannot serve as a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: an objection followed by a refutation.
2
Identify the claim being refuted
The objection states that the Prophet's unique knowledge of a certain drug would be a miracle. Identify this claim in the passage.
3
Understand the author's key argument
The author says that such unique knowledge is common (mu'tād) in every age—there is always someone who knows what others don't. This is the crucial point.
4
Connect to the definition of miracle
A miracle is defined as something that breaks the norm (khāriq li-l-'ādah). Since unique knowledge is common, it does not break the norm and thus is not a miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الرابع : وهو قوله : ( اختصاصه بمعرفة ذلك الدواء ، أن يكون معجزاً » فنقول : هذا باطل . لأن حصول إنسان في كل عصر يختص بمعرفة أشياء لا يعرفها غيره : أمر معتاد ، وإذا كان هذا معتاداً ، فقد خرج ذلك عن أن يكون معجزاً .
As for the answer to the fourth: which is his statement: 'His unique knowledge of that drug would be a miracle.' We say: This is false, because the existence in every age of a person who is uniquely knowledgeable of things that others do not know is a common occurrence. And if this is common, then it is excluded from being a miracle.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This refutes the claim that unique knowledge of a drug is a miracle. Since it is common for some people to know what others don't, it cannot be considered a miracle (which is extraordinary and breaks the norm).

Misconception: Unique knowledge is always a miracle.
Correction: The author shows that unique knowledge is common, so it cannot be a miracle unless it breaks the norm.

C) Because knowledge cannot be miraculous.
D) Because the drug itself is not miraculous.

Key Takeaway
Unique knowledge of a drug is not a miracle because it is a common occurrence for individuals to know things others don't.

Third Possibility: Jinn as Agents of Miracles
Presentation of the third possibility: jinn as agents of miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third possibility that the author raises against the argument from miracles for prophethood: that jinn or devils could be the agents of these extraordinary events.

Core Idea
If jinn can speak through possessed humans, why not through animals and even the Quran?

In this passage, the author presents a challenging possibility: the miracles attributed to prophets might actually be the work of jinn or devils. He builds his case on the widespread belief in jinn and their abilities, and then draws analogies to commonly accepted phenomena like possession. This raises a serious doubt about the certainty that miracles come from God alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage and identify the central possibility being proposed: that jinn or devils could be the agents of miracles.
This is the 'third possibility'.
2
Examine the premise
Notice that the author claims people unanimously agree on the existence of jinn and their ability to do things humans cannot. This premise makes the possibility plausible.
3
Follow the logical inference
If jinn can do extraordinary things, then it is not impossible that miracles are their work. The author asks how we can be certain otherwise.
This challenges the standard view.
4
Analyze the analogy with possession
The author points out that people accept jinn entering humans and speaking through them. So why not accept that talking animals and even the Quran could be from jinn?
This extends the argument to all miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتمال الثالث : أن يقال : إن أرباب الملل والنحل أطبقوا على إثبات الجن والشياطين ، واتفقوا على أنهم يقدرون على الإتيان بما يعجز عنه البشر . وأيضاً : فهب أن أرباب الملل لم يتفقوا على هذا المعنى ، إلا أن تجويزه قائم في أول العقل . وإذا كان كذلك ، فبتقدير أن يصح ذلك ، لم يمتنع [ ان يصح ] أن يكون الفاعل لهذه المعجزات واحداً من الجن ، أو الشياطين . ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، كيف يمكن الجزم بأن فاعل هذه المعجزات هو الله تعالى ؟ والعجب : أن الناس يجوزون دخول الجني في بدن المصروع ، ويجوزون أن يتكلم [ الجني على لسان المصروع ] وأنه يخبر عن الغيوب على لسان المصروع . فلما جوزوا ذلك ، فلم لا يجوزون أن الذئب لما تكلم مع الرسول عليه السلام ، أو الجمل [ لما تكلم معه ] أو الذراع المسموم لما تكلم معه ، فذلك الكلام إنما حصل لأجل [ أن الجني نفذ في بطن ذلك ] الذئب والجمل والذراع وتكلم ؟ ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، فكيف قطعوا بأنه معجز حصل بخلق الله تعالى ؟
وأيضاً
ولم لا يجوزون أن يقال : إن انقلاب العصا حية ، كان من هذا الباب ؟ : فلم لا يجوزون أن [ يقال : إن ] فصاحة الجن ومردة الشياطين كانت وافية بمثل فصاحة القرآن ، فأتوا بهذا القرآن من عند أنفسهم ، وألقوه
The third possibility: that it be said: The people of religions and sects have unanimously agreed upon the existence of jinn and devils, and they have agreed that they are able to do what humans are incapable of. Also, even if the people of religions did not agree on this meaning, the possibility of it is established in the first principles of intellect. And if this is so, then assuming that it is correct, it is not impossible [that] the agent of these miracles could be one of the jinn or devils. And with this possibility present, how can one be certain that the agent of these miracles is God Almighty? And it is astonishing that people allow the entry of a jinn into the body of a possessed person, and they allow the jinn to speak on the tongue of the possessed, and that it informs of hidden matters on the tongue of the possessed. Since they permit that, why do they not permit that the wolf that spoke to the Prophet (peace be upon him), or the camel [that spoke to him], or the poisoned foreleg that spoke to him, that speech occurred because the jinn entered into the belly of that wolf, camel, and foreleg and spoke? And with this possibility present, how have they been certain that it is a miracle that occurred by the creation of God Almighty? And also: Why do they not allow that it be said: The transformation of the staff into a serpent was of this type? So why do they not allow that the eloquence of the jinn and the rebellious devils was sufficient for an eloquence like that of the Quran, so they produced this Quran from themselves, and they cast it...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents a third possibility against using miracles as proof of prophethood: that jinn or devils could be the agents of these extraordinary events. The author points out that people commonly accept that jinn can enter humans and speak through them, so why not accept that the talking animals and other miracles were also performed by jinn? The Quran itself might be attributed to the eloquence of jinn. This raises a serious objection that undermines the certainty that miracles come from God.

Answer to the Fourth Objection: Special Knowledge as a Miracle
Sanusi refutes the fourth objection on miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi rejects the idea that a prophet's unique knowledge of a specific remedy qualifies as a miracle.

Core Idea
Unique knowledge is customary, not miraculous.

In this passage, Sanusi responds to the fourth objection against miracles. The objector claimed that a prophet's special knowledge of a specific medicine is itself a miracle. Sanusi refutes this by pointing out that such specialization is a common occurrence in every age. Therefore, it cannot be a miracle because miracles must break the natural order.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the structure: objection, rejection, reason, conclusion.
2
Understand the Objection
The objection claims that a prophet's unique knowledge of a remedy is miraculous. Ask yourself why someone might think that.
This objection likely arises from viewing extraordinary knowledge as a sign.
3
Analyze the Refutation
Sanusi says the claim is false because specialized knowledge in every age is customary. Identify the key term 'customary' (معتاد) and its role.
Customary means something that happens regularly in human experience.
4
Reflect on the Definition of Miracle
Connect this to the definition of a miracle: something that breaks the natural order. Since specialized knowledge is customary, it does not break that order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الرابع : وهو قوله : ( اختصاصه بمعرفة ذلك الدواء ، أن يكون معجزاً » فنقول : هذا باطل . لأن حصول إنسان في كل عصر يختص بمعرفة أشياء لا يعرفها غيره : أمر معتاد ، وإذا كان هذا معتاداً ، فقد خرج ذلك عن أن يكون معجزاً . فهذا تمام القول في هذا السؤال
And the answer to the fourth [objection]: which is his statement: 'His specialization in knowing that medicine makes it a miracle.' So we say: This is false. Because the existence of a person in every age who specializes in knowing things that others do not know is a customary matter. And if this is customary, then it is excluded from being a miracle. This completes the statement on this question.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage provides the answer to the fourth objection against miracles. The objection claimed that a prophet's unique knowledge of a specific remedy (e.g., a healing substance) qualifies as a miracle. Sanusi refutes this by arguing that it is not miraculous because it is a common occurrence: in every age, there are individuals who possess specialized knowledge unknown to others. Since this is a customary phenomenon, it cannot serve as a miracle because miracles must break the natural order. Thus, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
معجز
معتاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any unique knowledge is a miracle.
Correction: Only what is impossible by custom is a miracle; unique expertise is customary.

Checkpoint

A) Because such knowledge is impossible for humans.
B) Because it is a common and customary occurrence in every age.
C) Because only prophets have such knowledge.
D) Because the Qur'an denies it.

Key Takeaway
Specialized knowledge, even if unique, is not a miracle because it conforms to the customary pattern of human expertise.

The Third Possibility: Could Jinn or Devils Perform Miracles?
Sanusi presents the third possibility, an objection against miracles being divine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that jinn and devils could be the agents behind miracles, and why this poses a challenge to certainty of divine origin.

Core Idea
Jinnic power casts doubt on divine agency in miracles—unless refuted.

Sanusi presents a serious objection from those who affirm the existence of jinn and their extraordinary abilities. If jinn can do what humans cannot, then how can we be sure that the agents of miracles are not jinn or devils? This lesson walks through the objection and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the logic of the objection unfold.
2
Identify the key examples
Notice the specific examples: talking animals, the staff turning into a snake, and the Quran's eloquence. How do they support the objection?
These examples are meant to show that jinn could be responsible.
3
Understand the challenge
The objection claims that if jinn might be the agents, we cannot be certain that miracles are from God. Think about why this is a powerful challenge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتمال الثالث : أن يقال : إن أرباب الملل والنحل أطبقوا على إثبات الجن والشياطين ، واتفقوا على أنهم يقدرون على الإتيان بما يعجز عنه البشر . وأيضاً : فهب أن أرباب الملل لم يتفقوا على هذا المعنى ، إلا أن تجويزه قائم في أول العقل . وإذا كان كذلك ، فبتقدير أن يصح ذلك ، لم يمتنع أن يصح أن يكون الفاعل لهذه المعجزات واحداً من الجن ، أو الشياطين . ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، كيف يمكن الجزم بأن فاعل هذه المعجزات هو الله تعالى ؟ والعجب : أن الناس يجوزون دخول الجني في بدن المصروع ، ويجوزون أن يتكلم الجني على لسان المصروع وأنه يخبر عن الغيوب على لسان المصروع . فلما جوزوا ذلك ، فلم لا يجوزون أن الذئب لما تكلم مع الرسول عليه السلام ، أو الجمل لما تكلم معه أو الذراع المسموم لما تكلم معه ، فذلك الكلام إنما حصل لأجل أن الجني نفذ في بطن ذلك الذئب والجمل والذراع وتكلم ؟ ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، فكيف قطعوا بأنه معجز حصل بخلق الله تعالى ؟ وأيضاً : ولم لا يجوزون أن يقال : إن انقلاب العصا حية ، كان من هذا الباب ؟ فلم لا يجوزون أن يقال : إن فصاحة الجن ومردة الشياطين كانت وافية بمثل فصاحة القرآن ، فأتوا بهذا القرآن من عند أنفسهم ، وألقوه على الرسول ؟ ومع هذا الاحتمال ، فكيف يمكن القطع بأنها من فعل الله ؟ واعلم : أن هذا السؤال : قد ذكره الله تعالى في القرآن ، فقال في سورة الشعراء : ( وإنه لتنزيل رب العالمين، نزل به الروح الأمين ، على قلبك لتكون من المنذرين ) . ثم قال بعده : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين وما ينبغي لهم وما يستطيعون إنهم عن السمع المعزولون ، والتقدير : إنه لما ادعي أنه تنزيل رب العالمين ، نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبه . فكان قائلاً قال : ولم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه من تنزيل الشياطين ؟ فلهذا السبب قال : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين ، ثم إنه أجاب عنه بقوله : هل أنبئكم : على من تنزل الشياطين ؟ تنزل على كل أفاك أثيم . يلقون السمع ، وأكثرهم كاذبون . وستعرف حقيقة هذا الجواب بعد ذلك
The third possibility: that it is said: The followers of religions and sects have concurred in affirming jinn and devils, and agreed that they are able to do what humans are incapable of. Also: suppose the followers of religions did not agree on this meaning, yet its logical possibility exists in the first [principles] of reason. And if that is so, then if that [ability] is valid, it is not impossible that the agent of these miracles be one of the jinn or devils. And with this possibility standing, how can it be certain that the agent of these miracles is God? And amazing: people allow the entry of a jinn into the body of an epileptic, and allow that the jinn speaks on the tongue of the epileptic and informs of unseen things on his tongue. Since they allow that, why do they not allow that when the wolf spoke to the Messenger, or the camel spoke to him, or the poisoned foreleg spoke to him, that that speech occurred because a jinn entered the belly of that wolf, camel, and foreleg and spoke? And with this possibility standing, how have they decided that it is a miracle created by God? Also: why do they not allow that it be said that the turning of the staff into a snake was of this category? Why do they not allow that it be said that the eloquence of jinn and rebellious devils was sufficient to match the eloquence of the Qur'an, so they brought this Qur'an from themselves and cast it upon the Messenger? With this possibility, how can it be decided that it is from the act of God? And know: this question has been mentioned by God in the Qur'an, for He said in Surat ash-Shu'ara: 'And indeed it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, brought down by the Trustworthy Spirit, upon your heart to be of the warners.' Then He said after it: 'And it has not been brought down by the devils, nor is it fit for them, nor are they able; indeed they are barred from hearing.' And the interpretation: when it was claimed that it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, the Trustworthy Spirit brought it down upon his heart. Then there was a speaker who said: Why is it not allowed that it be said: it is from the revelation of the devils? For this reason He said: 'And it has not been brought down by the devils.' Then He answered it by His saying: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend? They descend upon every sinful liar. They cast hearing, and most of them are liars.' And you will know the reality of this answer after this.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a major objection against miracles: since jinn and devils are capable of extraordinary acts, why cannot they be the agents of what appear to be miracles? The objector notes that even religious groups affirm the existence of jinn and their power to do what humans cannot. Even if they didn't, reason alone allows that possibility. Given this, one cannot be certain that God is the direct agent. The objector further argues by analogy: people accept that jinn can enter bodies and speak through them, so why not accept that the talking wolf, camel, and poisoned meat were also jinn? Why not say the staff turning into a snake was jinnic? And why not claim that the Qur'an itself could have been produced by eloquent jinn and cast upon the Prophet? Sanusi then shows that the Qur'an itself addresses this objection. In Surat ash-Shu'ara, God affirms that the Qur'an is His revelation, not from devils, and that devils cannot do so—they only descend upon sinful liars. This answer, though stated, is said to be fully explained later. The lesson thus presents the objection and the beginning of the Qur'anic refutation.

Key Terms
جن
شياطين
معجز
فصاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection proves that miracles are definitely not from God.
Correction: The objection only shows a logical possibility, not certainty. It requires a refutation to restore certainty.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why might one doubt that miracles are from God?
A) Because jinn and devils are known to be able to do extraordinary things.
B) Because humans can also perform miracles.
C) Because the Qur'an says jinn cannot do anything.
D) Because all miracles are actually performed by devils.

Key Takeaway
The objection from jinnic ability challenges the certainty of divine miracles by presenting an alternative non-divine supernatural explanation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the objection that jinn might have authored the Qur'an, do you feel any internal resistance or unease? That feeling is your īmān stirring. Ask yourself: have you ever allowed even a sliver of doubt about the divine origin of the Qur'an to linger in your heart without actively seeking its refutation? What will you do today to strengthen your conviction that every letter of the Qur'an is from Allah?
?
The objection uses analogies that you may have accepted without thinking—like jinn possession. Have you ever attributed a puzzling event to 'jinn' or 'coincidence' without first considering whether it might be a sign from Allah? How can you train your mind to first turn to Allah when faced with the extraordinary, instead of defaulting to natural or supernatural explanations that distance you from Him?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment and He asks you: 'Did you truly believe that My signs were from Me, or did you entertain the possibility that they came from jinn or devils?' How would you answer? What steps are you taking right now to remove any such possibility from your heart and to live with unshakeable certainty in Allah's direct intervention in the world?

The Qur'anic Refutation: Miracles Are from God, Not Devils
Sanusi cites and explains Qur'anic verses that refute the possibility of devilish origin of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qur'anic answer to the objection, particularly the verses from Surat ash-Shu'ara that deny the devils' involvement.

Core Idea
The Qur'an explicitly denies that devils brought it, and states they only descend on sinful liars.

Having presented the objection, Sanusi now turns to the Qur'anic response. The Qur'an itself addresses the possibility of devilish origin in Surat ash-Shu'ara, affirming that it is a revelation from the Lord of the worlds, not from devils. This lesson unpacks these verses and their logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qur'anic verses and explanation
Read the Arabic passage including the verses. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: claim, objection, answer.
2
Understand the argument
The Qur'an first affirms the divine origin, then denies that devils could have brought it, then explains what kind of people devils descend upon.
3
See how the refutation works
The answer directly refutes the objection by showing that devils are incapable and only target liars. How does this restore certainty?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتمال الثالث : أن يقال : إن أرباب الملل والنحل أطبقوا على إثبات الجن والشياطين ، واتفقوا على أنهم يقدرون على الإتيان بما يعجز عنه البشر . وأيضاً : فهب أن أرباب الملل لم يتفقوا على هذا المعنى ، إلا أن تجويزه قائم في أول العقل . وإذا كان كذلك ، فبتقدير أن يصح ذلك ، لم يمتنع أن يصح أن يكون الفاعل لهذه المعجزات واحداً من الجن ، أو الشياطين . ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، كيف يمكن الجزم بأن فاعل هذه المعجزات هو الله تعالى ؟ والعجب : أن الناس يجوزون دخول الجني في بدن المصروع ، ويجوزون أن يتكلم الجني على لسان المصروع وأنه يخبر عن الغيوب على لسان المصروع . فلما جوزوا ذلك ، فلم لا يجوزون أن الذئب لما تكلم مع الرسول عليه السلام ، أو الجمل لما تكلم معه أو الذراع المسموم لما تكلم معه ، فذلك الكلام إنما حصل لأجل أن الجني نفذ في بطن ذلك الذئب والجمل والذراع وتكلم ؟ ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال ، فكيف قطعوا بأنه معجز حصل بخلق الله تعالى ؟ وأيضاً : ولم لا يجوزون أن يقال : إن انقلاب العصا حية ، كان من هذا الباب ؟ فلم لا يجوزون أن يقال : إن فصاحة الجن ومردة الشياطين كانت وافية بمثل فصاحة القرآن ، فأتوا بهذا القرآن من عند أنفسهم ، وألقوه على الرسول ؟ ومع هذا الاحتمال ، فكيف يمكن القطع بأنها من فعل الله ؟ واعلم : أن هذا السؤال : قد ذكره الله تعالى في القرآن ، فقال في سورة الشعراء : ( وإنه لتنزيل رب العالمين، نزل به الروح الأمين ، على قلبك لتكون من المنذرين ) . ثم قال بعده : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين وما ينبغي لهم وما يستطيعون إنهم عن السمع المعزولون ، والتقدير : إنه لما ادعي أنه تنزيل رب العالمين ، نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبه . فكان قائلاً قال : ولم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه من تنزيل الشياطين ؟ فلهذا السبب قال : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين ، ثم إنه أجاب عنه بقوله : هل أنبئكم : على من تنزل الشياطين ؟ تنزل على كل أفاك أثيم . يلقون السمع ، وأكثرهم كاذبون . وستعرف حقيقة هذا الجواب بعد ذلك
The third possibility: that it is said: The followers of religions and sects have concurred in affirming jinn and devils, and agreed that they are able to do what humans are incapable of. Also: suppose the followers of religions did not agree on this meaning, yet its logical possibility exists in the first [principles] of reason. And if that is so, then if that [ability] is valid, it is not impossible that the agent of these miracles be one of the jinn or devils. And with this possibility standing, how can it be certain that the agent of these miracles is God? And amazing: people allow the entry of a jinn into the body of an epileptic, and allow that the jinn speaks on the tongue of the epileptic and informs of unseen things on his tongue. Since they allow that, why do they not allow that when the wolf spoke to the Messenger, or the camel spoke to him, or the poisoned foreleg spoke to him, that that speech occurred because a jinn entered the belly of that wolf, camel, and foreleg and spoke? And with this possibility standing, how have they decided that it is a miracle created by God? Also: why do they not allow that it be said that the turning of the staff into a snake was of this category? Why do they not allow that it be said that the eloquence of jinn and rebellious devils was sufficient to match the eloquence of the Qur'an, so they brought this Qur'an from themselves and cast it upon the Messenger? With this possibility, how can it be decided that it is from the act of God? And know: this question has been mentioned by God in the Qur'an, for He said in Surat ash-Shu'ara: 'And indeed it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, brought down by the Trustworthy Spirit, upon your heart to be of the warners.' Then He said after it: 'And it has not been brought down by the devils, nor is it fit for them, nor are they able; indeed they are barred from hearing.' And the interpretation: when it was claimed that it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, the Trustworthy Spirit brought it down upon his heart. Then there was a speaker who said: Why is it not allowed that it be said: it is from the revelation of the devils? For this reason He said: 'And it has not been brought down by the devils.' Then He answered it by His saying: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend? They descend upon every sinful liar. They cast hearing, and most of them are liars.' And you will know the reality of this answer after this.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a major objection against miracles: since jinn and devils are capable of extraordinary acts, why cannot they be the agents of what appear to be miracles? The objector notes that even religious groups affirm the existence of jinn and their power to do what humans cannot. Even if they didn't, reason alone allows that possibility. Given this, one cannot be certain that God is the direct agent. The objector further argues by analogy: people accept that jinn can enter bodies and speak through them, so why not accept that the talking wolf, camel, and poisoned meat were also jinn? Why not say the staff turning into a snake was jinnic? And why not claim that the Qur'an itself could have been produced by eloquent jinn and cast upon the Prophet? Sanusi then shows that the Qur'an itself addresses this objection. In Surat ash-Shu'ara, God affirms that the Qur'an is His revelation, not from devils, and that devils cannot do so—they only descend upon sinful liars. This answer, though stated, is said to be fully explained later. The lesson thus presents the objection and the beginning of the Qur'anic refutation.

Key Terms
شياطين
تنزيل
الروح الأمين
أفاك أثيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an does not address the objection of jinnic or devilish origin of miracles.
Correction: The Qur'an explicitly addresses it in Surat ash-Shu'ara, denying that devils brought the revelation and stating their limitations.

Checkpoint
According to the Qur'anic passage, upon whom do the devils descend?
A) Upon prophets and messengers.
B) Upon every sinful liar.
C) Upon sincere believers.
D) Upon anyone who recites the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an refutes the objection by asserting that devils cannot produce revelation and only descend upon sinful liars, thus protecting its miraculous nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe the Qur'an is from God and not from any other source? What evidence from this passage strengthens your conviction? Are you willing to live by it even when it contradicts your desires?
?
The devils descend on every sinful liar. Does your life reflect the opposite? Are you a person of truthfulness and integrity so that you are far from the description of those whom devils influence? What specific step will you take today to increase your honesty?
?
If the Prophet Muhammad (s) was so protected from falsehood that devils could not influence him, how should that affect your trust in his message? Will you follow him in all matters, even the ones that are hard for you?

The Quraysh's Jinn Analogy and the Qur'anic Response
Sanusi explains how Quraysh used the poet-jinn companionship analogy to question prophetic miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quraysh used the poet-jinn relationship to question Muhammad's prophethood and how the Qur'an refuted it.

Core Idea
Poets have jinn helpers; the Quraysh argued Muhammad might too. The Qur'an contrasts prophets with poets.

The Quraysh, in their opposition to the Prophet, employed a clever cultural analogy. Among the Arabs, it was widely believed that every great poet had a jinn companion who inspired his verses. They extended this to the Prophet, asking: if poets have jinn helpers, why can't Muhammad's revelations come from a jinn? This passage from Sanusi presents that objection and the Qur'anic reply, setting the stage for a deeper discussion on the nature of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi introduces the Quraysh's reasoning as an 'emphasis' of a previous question.
2
Identify the analogy
The Quraysh argue from a known fact: every poet has a jinn companion. They apply this to the Prophet. Identify the steps in their logic.
The analogy is: poet : jinn :: Muhammad : ?
3
See the Qur'anic answer
The Qur'an responds by distinguishing prophets from poets: poets are followed by the misguided. This implies that prophetic guidance is different in nature.
The full explanation of the answer is deferred to later chapters.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Sanusi says the purpose is to show that this objection was famous from the beginning. Reflect on why it was important to address this early.
This shows the Qur'an and early Muslims were aware of and responded to these challenges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن كفار قريش كانوا يؤكدون هذا السؤال بوجه آخر ، فيقولون : إنه من المشهور عند جمهور العرب : أن لكل شاعر صاحباً من الجن يعينه على الشعر - ويهديه إلى دقائقه ، ويرشده إلى مضايقه . فقالوا لمحمد عليه السلام : لما كان هذا مشهوراً في حق الشعراء ، فلم يجوز مثله في حقك ؟ فأجاب عنه في آخر هذه الآيات بقوله : ( والشعراء يتبعهم الغاوون )، وستعرف حقيقة هذا الجواب في الفصول الأتية . والمقصود ههنا : بيان أن هذا السؤال مشهور ، مذكور من أول الأمر .
And know that the disbelievers of Quraysh used to emphasize this question in another way, saying: It is well-known among the majority of Arabs that every poet has a companion from the jinn who assists him in poetry, guides him to its subtleties, and directs him to its difficulties. So they said to Muhammad, peace be upon him: Since this is well-known regarding poets, why is not the like allowed regarding you? So He answered it at the end of these verses by His saying: 'And the poets, the misguided follow them.' And you will know the reality of this answer in the coming chapters. And the purpose here is to show that this question is famous, mentioned from the very beginning.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents another variant of the jinn-based objection, this time from the Quraysh. They argued: it is well-known that each Arab poet has a jinn companion who helps him compose poetry and guides him to its fine points. So why should not the same be true for Muhammad? Perhaps his revelations are merely from a jinn. The Qur'anic response is cited: 'And the poets, the misguided follow them' (ash-Shu'ara 224). The author notes that the full explanation of this answer will be given later; for now, the purpose is simply to show that this objection was widely known from the beginning of Islam. Thus, the passage highlights that the challenge of distinguishing prophetic revelation from jinnic inspiration was recognized and addressed in the Qur'an itself.

Key Terms
شعراء
جن
كفار قريش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophetic revelation is similar to poetic inspiration from jinn.
Correction: The Qur'an distinguishes the two: prophets bring guidance, while poets are followed by the misguided.

Checkpoint
What was the Quraysh's specific objection regarding jinn and the Prophet?
A) That jinn cannot help poets.
B) That Muhammad must have a jinn companion like poets do, so his revelation may not be divine.
C) That the Qur'an is actually poetry composed by Muhammad.
D) That the jinn are more powerful than God.

Key Takeaway
The Quraysh's objection based on poet-jinn companionship was answered by the Qur'an by distinguishing prophets from poets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quraysh dismissed the Prophet's message by drawing a familiar analogy to poets and jinn. What familiar analogies do you use to dismiss uncomfortable truths in your own life? Are you willing to investigate them instead of relying on surface comparisons?
?
When you read that 'poets, the misguided follow them,' do you feel the weight of taking guidance from sources that lead you astray? Who or what are you following, and on what basis?
?
The Prophet's answer did not come from him but from Allah. In moments of confusion, do you truly seek Allah's guidance, or do you rely on your own reasoning and the common opinions around you?

The Quranic Refutation of the Devilish Origin Claim
Author cites Quranic verses addressing the objection that the Quran could be from devils.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran itself anticipates and refutes the objection that it could be from devils, and how this refutation distinguishes the Quran from poetic inspiration.

Core Idea
The Quran's divine origin is defended directly within its own verses.

This lesson examines a passage where the author demonstrates that the question of the Quran being from devils was not a later innovation but was addressed in the Quran itself. By citing verses from Surah Ash-Shu'ara', the author shows the Quran's own arguments against this claim. The passage also tackles a related objection based on the Arab tradition of poets having jinn helpers, further clarifying the unique nature of Quranic revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main objection
The passage begins by noting that the question of devilish origin is mentioned in the Quran. Recognize that this objection is anticipated and not a later invention.
The author uses the phrase 'واعلم' to draw attention.
2
Examine the first Quranic refutation
The author cites verses 26:192-194 stating the Quran is a revelation from the Lord brought by the Trustworthy Spirit. Then verses 26:210-211 assert that devils do not bring it down.
3
Understand the second objection about poets
The Quraysh argued that poets have jinn helpers, so perhaps Muhammad had similar assistance. This is a second layer of the objection.
The author mentions this was a common belief among Arabs.
4
See the second Quranic response
The Quran responds with verse 26:224 that poets are followed by the erring, distinguishing the Quran from poetry and its sources.
The author notes the full explanation will come later.
5
Reflect on the author's purpose
The author concludes that the purpose is to show this question has been famous since the beginning, and the Quran already answered it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن هذا السؤال : قد ذكره الله تعالى في القرآن ، فقال في سورة الشعراء : ( وإنه لتنزيل رب العالمين، نزل به الروح الأمين ، على قلبك لتكون من المنذرين ). ثم قال بعده : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين [ وما ينبغي لهم وما يستطيعون إنهم عن السمع المعزولون ، والتقدير : [ إنه لما ادعي ] أنه تنزيل رب العالمين ، نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبه . فكان قائلاً قال : ولم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه من تنزيل الشياطين ؟ فلهذا السبب قال : « وما تنزلت به الشياطين ، ثم إنه أجاب عنه بقوله : هل أنبئكم : على من تنزل الشياطين ؟ تنزل على كل أفاك أثيم . يلقون السمع ، وأكثرهم كاذبون . وستعرف حقيقة هذا الجواب بعد ذلك. واعلم أن كفار قريش كانوا يؤكدون هذا السؤال بوجه آخر ، فيقولون : إنه من المشهور عند جمهور العرب : أن لكل شاعر صاحباً من الجن يعينه على الشعر - ويهديه إلى دقائقه ، ويرشده إلى مضايقه . فقالوا لمحمد عليه السلام : لما كان هذا مشهوراً في حق الشعراء ، فلم يجوز مثله في حقك ؟ فأجاب عنه في آخر هذه الآيات بقوله : ( والشعراء يتبعهم الغاوون، وستعرف حقيقة هذا الجواب في الفصول الأتية . والمقصود ههنا : بيان أن هذا السؤال مشهور ، مذكور من أول الأمر .
And know: that this question has been mentioned by Allah the Exalted in the Quran, for He said in Surat Ash-Shu'ara': (And indeed it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, brought down by the Trustworthy Spirit, upon your heart, that you may be among the warners). Then He said after it: 'And it is not the devils that have brought it down, nor does it behoove them, nor are they able. Indeed they are removed from hearing.' And the implied meaning: [When it was claimed] that it is a revelation of the Lord of the worlds, brought down by the Trustworthy Spirit upon his heart, someone said: Why is it not permissible to say that it is from the revelation of the devils? For this reason He said: 'And it is not the devils that have brought it down.' Then He answered it by His saying: 'Shall I inform you upon whom the devils descend? They descend upon every sinful liar. They pass on hearing, and most of them are liars.' And you will know the reality of this answer later. And know that the disbelievers of Quraysh used to emphasize this question in another way, saying: It is well-known among the majority of Arabs that every poet has a companion from the jinn who assists him in poetry, guides him to its subtleties, and directs him to its intricacies. So they said to Muhammad, peace be upon him: Since this is well-known regarding poets, why is the like of it not permissible in your case? He answered it at the end of these verses by His saying: 'And the poets are followed by the erring.' And you will know the reality of this answer in the coming chapters. And the purpose here is to show that this question is famous, mentioned from the beginning.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage demonstrates that the objection attributing the Quran to devils was anticipated and refuted in the Quran itself. The author first cites Surah Ash-Shu'ara' (26:192-194) to establish that the Quran is a revelation from the Lord of the worlds, brought by the Trustworthy Spirit (Jibril). He then explains the logical progression: since it is claimed as revelation from Allah, one might ask why it could not be from devils. The Quran responds by stating that devils do not bring down revelation (26:210-211) and that they descend only upon sinful liars (26:221-223). The author then notes that the Quraysh raised a further objection based on the Arab tradition that poets have jinn helpers, implying that Muhammad could also have such assistance. The Quran refutes this by stating that poets are followed by the erring (26:224), distinguishing the Quranic revelation from poetry. The author concludes that the purpose of this discussion is to show that this question has been well-known since the beginning.

Misconception: One might think the question of devilish origin is a later innovation or not addressed in the Quran.

C) 'And the poets are followed by the erring'
D) 'It is not the devils that have brought it down'

Key Takeaway
The Quran's own verses defend its divine origin by excluding the possibility of devilish intervention and distinguishing it from poetic inspiration.

?
The Quraysh dismissed the Quran by comparing it to poetry inspired by jinn. What modern analogies do people in your life use to dismiss or undermine your trust in the Quran? Are you ever swayed by them, even slightly?
?
The Quran distinguishes between those who follow the truth and those who follow erring poets. Which company do you keep, and does your choice of companions reflect a love for divine guidance or a comfort with worldly admiration?

Three Objections to Miracles Being from Jinn and Their Refutation
Author presents and refutes three objections to miracles being from jinn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three objections raised against the possibility of miracles being performed by jinn and the author's refutation of each, demonstrating the weakness of these objections.

Core Idea
Objections to jinn miracles are refuted by logical and prophetic evidence.

In this passage, the author addresses skeptics who deny that miracles could be from jinn by presenting three common objections. Each objection is shown to be weak through rational argument and reference to prophetic statements. This lesson helps you follow the reasoning behind each refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and objections
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow: three objections followed by three refutations.
Notice the structure: 'فإن قالوا... قلنا' pattern for each objection.
2
Analyze the first objection and refutation
The first objection: prophets curse jinn, so how can jinn assist? The refutation: jinn may tolerate cursing to preserve deceptions, or the cursed group may differ from those performing miracles.
3
Analyze the second objection and refutation
The second objection: if jinn did miracles, Allah would have to support a sinner to avoid confusion. The refutation: the possibility of jinn involvement means certainty of divine origin is unwarranted, similar to ambiguous verses.
This parallels the concept of ambiguous verses (mutashabihat).
4
Analyze the third objection and refutation
The third objection: jinn lack power for great miracles. The refutation: prophets affirm jinn's great power, so denying it would accuse prophets of falsehood.
This is a powerful argument from prophetic testimony.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the author systematically dismantles each objection, showing that the possibility of jinn involvement remains logically and theologically viable.
The key is that the objections are based on assumptions that are not necessarily true.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : هذا مدفوع من وجوه : الأول : إن الأنبياء عليهم السلام ، إنما جاؤا بلعن الشياطين والجن والأبالسة ، فكيف يعقل كون الأبالسة أعواناً لهم في تقرير المعجزات ؟ والثاني : إنه لو فعل الجني ذلك ، لوجب على الله تعالى أن ينصر إنساناً يأتي بمعاصيه ، لئلا يحصل التلبيس . وحيث لم يفعل ، علمنا أنه ليس من فعل الجن ، بل من فعل الله تعالى . الثالث : إن الجن لم يبلغوا في القدرة إلى هذا الحد العظيم . إذ لو قدروا عليه ، لوجب أن يصل منهم الشر العظيم إلى الأنبياء والعلماء الذين يشتغلون بلعنهم ، وسوء القول فيهم . قلنا : أما الجواب الأول فضعيف : لأنه لا يبعد أن يقال : إنهم لشدة رغبتهم في إبقاء الشبهات والأباطيل ، يتحملون ذلك الطعن واللعن ، ومع ذلك فيعينون هؤلاء الدعاة على سبيل الكذب، ليحصل غرضهم من ترويج هذه الشبهات . وأيضاً : فلعل المراد بهذا اللعن : طائفة والأتون بهذه المعجزات : أقوم آخرون . وأما الجواب الثاني : فضعيف أيضاً . لأنه مع قيام هذا الاحتمال أعني كون هذه المعجزات أفعالاً للجن . لو جزم المكلف بكونها صادرة من الله تعالى ، لكان التقصير من المكلف ، حيث جزم لا في موضع الجزم . وهذا كما قلنا : في إنزال الآيات المتشابهة ، فإنها وإن كانت عظيمة الإبهام لهذه الأباطيل ، إلا أنه لم يقبح صدورها من الله تعالى ، لقيام الاحتمال فيها ، فكذا مهنا . وأما الجواب الثالث فضعيف : لأن الأنبياء عليهم السلام أطبقوا على إثبات القوة العظيمة لهم . فإنكار هذه القوة يوجب تكذيب الأنبياء . وذلك من أعظم المطاعن في نبوتهم .
For if they say: This is refuted in ways: First: The prophets, peace be upon them, only came with cursing of devils, jinn, and satans, so how can it be rational that the satans are their assistants in establishing miracles? Second: If the jinn had done that, then Allah the Exalted would have to support a man who commits disobediences with it, so that confusion does not occur. And since He did not, we know that it is not from the act of the jinn, but from the act of Allah the Exalted. Third: The jinn have not reached in power to this great extent. For if they were able to do it, then great evil would necessarily reach the prophets and scholars who engage in cursing them and speaking ill of them. We say: As for the first answer, it is weak: because it is not far-fetched to say that due to their intense desire to preserve doubts and falsehoods, they bear that insult and curse, and yet they assist these callers on the path of lying, to achieve their goal of promoting these doubts. Also: perhaps what is meant by this curse is a group, and those who bring these miracles are other people. As for the second answer, it is also weak. Because with the existence of this possibility, namely that these miracles are acts of the jinn, if the responsible person were certain that they proceed from Allah the Exalted, then the shortcoming would be from the responsible person, since he is certain where certainty is not warranted. And this is like we said regarding the revelation of ambiguous verses: for although they are great in obscuring these falsehoods, yet it is not evil from Allah the Exalted that they proceed, due to the existence of possibility in them, so too here. As for the third answer, it is weak: because the prophets, peace be upon them, have unanimously affirmed great power for them. Denying this power necessitates calling the prophets liars. And that is one of the greatest objections to their prophethood.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents three objections to the idea that miracles could be performed by jinn, and then refutes each. The first objection argues that since prophets curse devils and jinn, it is irrational for devils to assist them. The author dismisses this as weak: the jinn might tolerate the cursing to preserve their deceptions, or the group cursed may be different from those performing the miracles. The second objection claims that if jinn did miracles, Allah would have to support a sinner to avoid confusion; since He does not, the miracle must be from Allah. The author counters that the possibility of jinn involvement means that being certain of divine origin without justification is the fault of the believer, not of Allah — analogous to how ambiguous verses can be sent despite possible misinterpretation. The third objection asserts that jinn lack the power to perform great miracles, otherwise they would harm prophets and scholars. The author refutes this by noting that prophets themselves affirm the great power of jinn, so denying it would accuse prophets of falsehood, which is a major flaw in prophethood. Thus all three objections are shown to be weak.

Key Terms
جبالسة
تلبيس
معجزات
إبهام
شبهات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objections against jinn involvement in miracles are conclusive and prove that miracles must be from Allah alone.
Correction: The author shows that each objection is weak and that the possibility of jinn involvement remains logically and theologically viable.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against the second objection (that if jinn did miracles, Allah would have to support a sinner)?
A) Jinn are incapable of such acts
B) The possibility of jinn involvement makes certainty about divine origin unjustified, so the fault lies with the believer
C) Allah does support sinners sometimes
D) The objection is based on a misunderstood verse

Key Takeaway
The three objections to jinn miracles are refuted by logical reasoning and prophetic testimony, showing that the possibility of jinn involvement remains valid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim about someone performing a miracle, how do you determine whether it is from Allah or from other sources? Do you require full certainty before accepting it, or do you leave room for possibility? How does the author's discussion of 'certainty where certainty is not warranted' challenge your own approach to such situations?
?
The author suggests that jinn might bear curses and insults to preserve their deceptions. Are there areas in your life where you endure discomfort or criticism to maintain a false belief or practice? What would it take for you to honestly examine whether your persistence is for truth or for self-deception?
?
If you were to deny the great power of jinn that the prophets affirmed, you would be indirectly accusing the prophets of falsehood. How careful are you to ensure that your theological opinions are consistent with what the prophets taught, even when those opinions seem plausible? What steps can you take to align your beliefs more closely with prophetic teachings?

Refutation of Three Objections Against Jinn Miracles
Objections that jinn cannot perform miracles are answered and shown weak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical scholars defend the possibility of jinn performing miracles by refuting three key objections based on logical and textual reasoning.

Core Idea
Miracles can be performed by jinn without undermining prophethood, as objections are based on weak assumptions.

This passage addresses three objections raised against the idea that jinn could perform miracles. The author systematically refutes each, showing that the objections rely on flawed reasoning. By examining these refutations, we gain insight into the theological defense of miracles and the role of jinn in Islamic cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Objections
Read the passage carefully and list the three objections raised against jinn performing miracles. Notice the logical structure of each objection.
The objections are introduced with 'First', 'Second', and 'Third'.
2
Understand the First Refutation
Focus on the response to the first objection about prophets cursing devils. How does the author argue that devils might still assist despite being cursed?
The key is the devils' intense desire to spread falsehood.
3
Analyze the Second Refutation
Examine the second answer regarding probability and certainty. Why does the author say that mere possibility prevents absolute certainty?
Compare with the example of ambiguous Quranic verses.
4
Examine the Third Refutation
Look at the third answer about jinn's limited power. How does the author use the prophets' own testimony to refute this objection?
Denying jinn's power would contradict the prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : هذا مدفوع من وجوه : الأول : إن الأنبياء عليهم السلام ، إنما جاؤوا بلعن الشياطين والجن والأبالسة ، فكيف يعقل كون الأبالسة أعواناً لهم في تقرير المعجزات ؟ والثاني : إنه لو فعل الجني ذلك ، لوجب على الله تعالى أن ينصر إنساناً يأتي بمعاصيه ، لئلا يحصل التلبيس . وحيث لم يفعل ، علمنا أنه ليس من فعل الجن ، بل من فعل الله تعالى . الثالث : إن الجن لم يبلغوا في القدرة إلى هذا الحد العظيم . إذ لو قدروا عليه ، لوجب أن يصل منهم الشر العظيم إلى الأنبياء والعلماء الذين يشتغلون بلعنهم ، وسوء القول فيهم .
قلنا : أما الجواب الأول فضعيف : لأنه لا يبعد أن يقال : إنهم لشدة رغبتهم في إبقاء الشبهات والأباطيل ، يتحملون ذلك الطعن واللعن ، ومع ذلك فيعينون هؤلاء الدعاة على سبيل الكذب، ليحصل غرضهم من ترويج هذه الشبهات . وأيضاً : فلعل المراد بهذا اللعن : طائفة والأتون بهذه المعجزات : أقوم آخرون .
وأما الجواب الثاني : فضعيف أيضاً . لأنه مع قيام هذا الاحتمال أعني كون هذه المعجزات أفعالاً للجن . لو جزم المكلف بكونها صادرة من الله تعالى ، لكان التقصير من المكلف، حيث جزم لا في موضع الجزم . وهذا كما قلنا : في إنزال الآيات المتشابهة، فإنها وإن كانت عظيمة الإبهام لهذه الأباطيل، إلا أنه لم يقبح صدورها من الله تعالى، لقيام الاحتمال فيها، فكذا هنا .
وأما الجواب الثالث فضعيف : لأن الأنبياء عليهم السلام أطبقوا على إثبات القوة العظيمة لهم . فإنكار هذه القوة يوجب تكذيب الأنبياء . وذلك من أعظم المطاعن في نبوتهم .
If they say: This is rebutted from several aspects: First: The prophets, peace be upon them, came only cursing devils, jinn, and satans, so how can it be rational that satans are helpers for them in establishing miracles? Second: If the jinn had done that, it would have been obligatory upon God Almighty to support a person who disobeys Him, lest confusion occur. Since He did not do so, we know that it is not from the act of jinn, but from the act of God Almighty. Third: The jinn have not reached such great power. For if they were capable of it, then great evil would have befallen the prophets and scholars who occupy themselves with cursing them and speaking ill of them.
We say: As for the first answer, it is weak: because it is not far-fetched to say that they, due to their intense desire to keep doubts and falsehoods, bear that insult and curse, and nevertheless they help these callers in a lying manner, so that their goal of promoting these doubts is achieved. Also, perhaps what is meant by this curse is a group, and those who come with these miracles are other people.
As for the second answer, it is also weak: because with the existence of this possibility—namely, that these miracles are acts of jinn—if the morally responsible person were certain that they proceed from God Almighty, the shortcoming would be from that person, since he made a certainty where certainty is not warranted. This is as we said regarding the sending down of ambiguous verses: even though they are great in their obscurity for these falsehoods, their occurrence from God Almighty is not deemed bad because of the existence of probability in them. So too here.
As for the third answer, it is weak: because the prophets, peace be upon them, have unanimously affirmed for them [the jinn] great power. Denying this power necessitates the denial of the prophets, and that is among the greatest objections to their prophethood.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents three objections raised by opponents against the claim that miracles could be performed by jinn, and then the author refutes each objection in turn. The first objection argues that prophets curse devils and jinn, so it is absurd that these same devils would aid the prophets by producing miracles. The author replies that the devils' desire to spread falsehood is so strong that they are willing to endure curses, and they might even assist lying claimants to achieve their goals. Moreover, the curse might be directed at one group while the miracles are performed by different beings. The second objection states that if a jinni performed a miracle, God should intervene to expose the deception by supporting someone who disobeys Him; since He does not, we know miracles are from God alone. The author counters that the mere possibility of jinnic involvement does not justify certainty that the act is from God; if someone is certain without removing that possibility, the fault lies with that person, just as ambiguous Quranic verses do not become evil because they can be misinterpreted. The third objection claims that jinn lack such great power, otherwise they would harm the prophets and scholars who curse them. The author responds that the prophets themselves affirmed the great power of jinn, so denying it would mean denying the prophets, which undermines the very claim of prophethood.

Key Terms
جن (jinn)
معجزات (miracles)
لعن (curse)
شبهات (doubts)
تلبيس (confusion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if jinn can perform miracles, then prophethood is unreliable because miracles could be faked.
Correction: The passage shows that objections against jinnic miracles are based on weak reasoning, and the possibility of jinn agency does not undermine the authenticity of prophethood, as other evidence establishes certainty.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main response to the first objection that prophets curse devils, so devils cannot help them?
A) The devils are forced by God to help
B) The devils tolerate the curse because they are eager to spread doubt and falsehood
C) The curse is only metaphorical
D) The prophets do not actually curse the devils

Key Takeaway
The three objections against jinn performing miracles are refuted through logical and textual arguments, preserving the integrity of prophethood and the possibility of jinnic agency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief that contradicts what you hold true, do you immediately dismiss it or do you examine the possibility that it might be correct—even if only in part? This lesson shows that mere possibility does not overturn certainty. Where in your life have you been certain without having such full certainty?
?
The passage says that if you claim certainty where only probability exists, the shortcoming is yours. Can you recall a time you were absolutely sure about something—a person's intention, an outcome, a doctrine—only to later discover you were mistaken? What would it mean for you to hold your beliefs with humility because of this lesson?
?
The prophets affirmed the great power of jinn even while cursing them. Is there someone you oppose—personally, politically, or religiously—whose strengths you can honestly acknowledge without feeling compromised? What would change in your heart if you could affirm their abilities while still disagreeing with them?

Fourth Objection: Angels as Miracle Agents and the Need for Infallibility
Fourth objection that angels could perform miracles, and answer showing dependence on transmitted proof of infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth objection to miracles as proof of prophethood—that angels could perform them—and why this objection leads to reliance on transmitted proofs for angelic infallibility.

Core Idea
Miracles lose evidential power unless we have independent proof that angels are infallible.

This passage presents a sophisticated theological objection: if angels, who are powerful and deliver revelation, could also perform miracles, then miracles no longer uniquely authenticate prophets. The answer, though incomplete here, points to a crucial dependence: we need to know angels are infallible, and that knowledge comes only from revelation—not reason. This sets up a circularity that the author will later address.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the claim that angels could be miracle-workers, supported by widespread belief and Quranic verses.
The objectors argue that since angels have great power, they could produce miracles.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites verses about Gabriel's power in destroying Lot's people and delivering the Quran. Identify how these verses support the objection.
Verses include 2:97, 26:193-194, 81:17-19, 53:5-6.
3
Grasp the conditional
The author states that before we know angels are infallible, miracles could be their doing. This conditional undermines the evidential value of miracles.
If angels are not known to be truthful, miracles could be used to support false prophets.
4
Identify the key claim about infallibility
The author asserts that knowledge of angelic infallibility comes only from transmitted proofs (naqli), not rational proofs.
This is a crucial move: reason alone cannot establish angelic truthfulness.
5
Notice the emerging circularity
The passage shows that transmitted proofs depend on prophetic truthfulness, which miracles are supposed to prove. This hints at a logical circle.
The passage cuts off before resolving the circle.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتمال الرابع : قالوا : أكثر أهل الدنيا أطبقوا على إثبات الملائكة والقرآن دل على أن بعد الإيمان بالله تعالى، لا يجب الإيمان بشيء آخر، إلا بالملائكة . فقال : « والمؤمنون كل من آمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله (۱) والقرآن دل أيضاً : على أنهم أصحاب القدر الظاهرة ، والقوى الغالبة ، فإن جبريل عليه السلام قلع مدائن قوم لوط من قعور الأرض ، ورفعها إلى قريب من السماء ، ثم رماها على الأرض. وأيضاً : القرآن (٢) يدل على أن القرآن إنما وصل إلى محمد عليه السلام من قبل جبريل ، فإنه قال : « قل من كان عدواً لجبريل ، فإنه نزله على قلبك (۳) وقال في سورة الشعراء : ه نزل به الروح الأمين . على قلبك (4) ، وقال : ( والليل إذا عسعس ، والصبح إذا تنفس ، إنه لقول رسول كريم (٥) ، [ فبين أن هذا القرآن إنما وصل إلى محمد عليه السلام بواسطة رسول كريم (۱) ] وقال أيضاً : علمـه شـديـد القــوى . ذو مـــرة فاستوی (۷).
إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إنا قبل العلم بعصمة الملائكة عن القبائح والأكاذيب والأضاليل ، نجوز أن تكون هذه المعجزات ، وإنما ظهرت على الأنبياء من قبلهم وبإعانتهم، وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يبقى في هذه المعجزات فائدة البتة ، ما لم نعلم كون الملائكة معصومين من الأباطيل والأكاذيب والعلم بعضمتهم لا يحصل من الدلائل العقلية ، بل من الدلائل النقلية . فعلى هذا يتوقف حصول العلم [ بعصمتهم على العلم (۸) ] بصحة الدلائل النقلية 1 والعلم بصحة الدلائل النقلية يتوقف على (۹) ] العلم بصدق الرسل ، في ادعاء
The fourth possibility: They said: Most people in the world have agreed upon the affirmation of angels, and the Qur'an indicates that after belief in God Almighty, one must not believe in anything else except the angels. He said: 'And the believers, each one believes in God, His angels, His books, and His messengers' (2:285). The Qur'an also indicates that they possess manifest power and overwhelming strength, for Gabriel, peace be upon him, uprooted the cities of Lot's people from the depths of the earth, raised them near the sky, and then threw them to the earth. Also, the Qur'an indicates that the Qur'an reached Muhammad, peace be upon him, only through Gabriel. He said: 'Say: Whoever is an enemy to Gabriel, indeed it is he who sent it down upon your heart' (2:97). And in Surah Ash-Shu'ara': 'The Trustworthy Spirit brought it down upon your heart' (26:193-194). And He said: 'By the night when it retreats, and the dawn when it breathes, indeed it is the word of a noble messenger' (81:17-19). [Thus it is made clear that this Qur'an only reached Muhammad, peace be upon him, through a noble messenger.] And He also said: 'He taught him, the one of great power, one of soundness, and he settled' (53:5-6).
If you understand this, we say: Before knowledge of the infallibility of angels from vile deeds, lies, and deceptions, we allow that these miracles could have appeared through the prophets by their agency and assistance. On this assumption, there remains no benefit in these miracles at all, unless we know that the angels are infallible from falsehoods and lies. And knowledge of their infallibility is not obtained from rational proofs, but from transmitted proofs. Therefore, the attainment of knowledge of their infallibility depends on knowledge of the validity of transmitted proofs, and knowledge of the validity of transmitted proofs depends on knowledge of the truthfulness of the messengers in their claim.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection and its partial answer. The objectors argue that angels, as established by widespread belief and the Qur'an, possess immense power and are the agents of revelation. Therefore, miracles could be their actions, not exclusively God's. The author then offers an answer: before we know that angels are infallible (ma'sum) from falsehood and deception, we cannot be sure that miracles are not angelic acts. If they could be, then miracles lose their evidential value, because the same signs could come from an angel to support a false prophet. The knowledge of angelic infallibility is not derived from rational proofs but from transmitted (naqli) proofs—i.e., revelation and tradition. This creates a circular dependence: knowledge of infallibility depends on the validity of transmitted proofs, and the validity of transmitted proofs depends on the truthfulness of the prophets. The passage ends abruptly, but the argument highlights the need for a foundational criterion to break the circle.

Key Terms
ملائكة (angels)
عصمة (infallibility)
دلائل نقلية (transmitted proofs)
دلائل عقلية (rational proofs)
رسل (messengers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this passage denies angelic infallibility.
Correction: The passage does not deny infallibility; it argues that rational proof alone cannot establish it—only revelation can.

Checkpoint
According to the author, knowledge of angelic infallibility depends on what?
A) Rational proofs alone
B) Transmitted proofs such as revelation and tradition
C) Direct observation
D) Consensus of scholars only

Key Takeaway
Even if miracles are possible through angels, their evidential value for prophethood depends on prior knowledge of angelic infallibility, which only revelation can provide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about miraculous events attributed to holy people, do you instinctively accept them or doubt them? What does this passage teach you about the need to rely on transmitted knowledge rather than your own rational assessment?
?
If the infallibility of angels can only be known through revelation, how does that affect your confidence in the Qur'an? Is your faith in the Qur'an based on rational arguments or on a deeper submission to God's word?
?
This passage shows a logical circle: miracles depend on transmitted proofs, and transmitted proofs depend on messengers. Where do you personally break that circle? Are you willing to accept the truthfulness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as starting point, or do you keep seeking a rational foundation?

The Quranic Foundation of Belief in Angels
Author cites Quranic verses to establish belief in angels and their power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic basis for the necessity of belief in angels and their extraordinary power and role in revelation.

Core Idea
Quran commands belief in angels and shows their might and role in delivering revelation.

Before engaging with the circularity argument, the author first establishes what the Quran teaches about angels. This passage collects several Quranic verses that demonstrate the necessity of believing in angels, their overwhelming power, and their role in delivering the Quran to the Prophet. Understanding this foundation is essential before proceeding to the logical problem that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the Quranic quotations. Notice how the author uses these verses to establish three points: belief in angels is obligatory, they possess immense power, and they are the intermediaries of revelation.
The verses are from Surah al-Baqarah, al-Shu'ara, and others.
2
Identify the three claims
Identify the three distinct claims the author makes using the verses: (1) belief in angels is required after belief in God, (2) angels have manifest power (e.g., Gabriel uproots cities), (3) the Quran was delivered by angels (Gabriel, the Trustworthy Spirit, a noble messenger).
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the author starts with these Quranic proofs. They establish that angels are central to Islamic creed and that miracles may be attributed to them, which is necessary for the upcoming circularity argument.
This lesson sets the stage for the next lesson on circularity.

والقرآن دل على أن بعد الإيمان بالله تعالى، لا يجب الإيمان بشيء آخر، إلا بالملائكة. فقال: (والمؤمنون كل من آمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله) والقرآن دل أيضاً: على أنهم أصحاب القدر الظاهرة، والقوى الغالبة، فإن جبريل عليه السلام قلع مدائن قوم لوط من قعور الأرض، ورفعها إلى قريب من السماء، ثم رماها على الأرض. وأيضاً: القرآن يدل على أن القرآن إنما وصل إلى محمد عليه السلام من قبل جبريل، فإنه قال: (قل من كان عدواً لجبريل، فإنه نزله على قلبك) وقال في سورة الشعراء: (نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبك) وقال: (والليل إذا عسعس، والصبح إذا تنفس، إنه لقول رسول كريم) فبين أن هذا القرآن إنما وصل إلى محمد عليه السلام بواسطة رسول كريم. وقال أيضاً: (علمه شديد القوى ذو مرة فاستوى). إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: إنا قبل العلم بعصمة الملائكة عن القبائح والأكاذيب والأضاليل، نجوز أن تكون هذه المعجزات، وإنما ظهرت على الأنبياء من قبلهم وبإعانتهم، وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يبقى في هذه المعجزات فائدة البتة، ما لم نعلم كون الملائكة معصومين من الأباطيل والأكاذيب. والعلم بعصمتهم لا يحصل من الدلائل العقلية، بل من الدلائل النقلية. فعلى هذا يتوقف حصول العلم بعصمتهم على العلم بصحة الدلائل النقلية. والعلم بصحة الدلائل النقلية يتوقف على العلم بصدق الرسل في ادعاء الرسالة. والعلم بصدقهم يتوقف على عصمة الملائكة، وذلك دور، والدور باطل.
The Quran indicated that after belief in God Almighty, one must not believe in anything else except the angels. He said: (And the believers, each one believes in God, His angels, His books, and His messengers) (2:285). And the Quran also indicated that they possess manifest power and overwhelming strength, for Gabriel (peace be upon him) uprooted the cities of the people of Lot from the depths of the earth and raised them near the sky, then threw them to the earth. Also, the Quran indicates that the Quran only reached Muhammad (peace be upon him) from Gabriel, for He said: (Say: whoever is an enemy to Gabriel – indeed he has brought it down upon your heart) (2:97). And He said in Surah al-Shu'ara: (The Trustworthy Spirit has brought it down upon your heart) (26:193-194). And He said: (By the night when it darkens, and by the dawn when it breathes, indeed it is the word of a noble messenger) (81:17-19). So He made clear that this Quran only reached Muhammad (peace be upon him) through a noble messenger. And He also said: (Taught by one of great power, of great strength, then he proceeded) (53:5-6). When you have understood this, we say: Before knowledge of the infallibility of angels from abominations, lies, and misguidances, we can allow that these miracles [appearing by the hands of prophets] could be from them and with their assistance. On this assumption, there remains no benefit in these miracles at all, unless we know that the angels are infallible from falsehoods and lies. Knowledge of their infallibility is not obtained from rational proofs, but rather from transmitted proofs. Thus the attainment of knowledge of their infallibility depends on knowledge of the validity of transmitted proofs. And knowledge of the validity of transmitted proofs depends on knowledge of the truthfulness of the messengers in their claim of prophethood. And knowledge of their truthfulness depends on the infallibility of the angels. That is a circle, and a circle is invalid.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the infallibility of angels cannot be rationally known, leading to circular reasoning if one attempts to prove prophethood through miracles. The author first establishes from the Quran the necessity of belief in angels and their power. Then he argues that if we do not already know angels are infallible, miracles could be attributed to them, making miracles useless as proof of prophethood. The only way to know angelic infallibility is through revelation, but revelation's validity depends on prophet's truthfulness, which in turn depends on miracles, which require angelic infallibility. Thus a vicious circle arises. The author concludes that this circle is invalid, implying that angelic infallibility must be known through other means.

Key Terms
الملائكة
جبريل
الروح الأمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first thing required after belief in God?
A) Belief in angels
B) Belief in books
C) Belief in messengers
D) Belief in predestination

Key Takeaway
The Quran establishes belief in angels as obligatory and attests to their power and role in revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in Allah, but do you truly believe in His angels with the same certainty? The Quran makes belief in angels a non-negotiable part of faith, right after belief in God. Examine your daily life: How often do you think about the angels who record your deeds, the ones who deliver revelation, or the ones who carry out Allah's commands? If your belief in angels is vague or forgotten, what will you do today to make it a living reality in your heart? Start by thanking Allah for sending the Quran through Gabriel, and ask yourself: Am I grateful enough for this blessing?
?
The passage shows that Gabriel, by Allah's command, literally uprooted entire cities and hurled them from the sky. This means the angels are not just passive spiritual beings—they are agents of immense power. Reflect: Does this reality affect how you view the unseen world? Are you aware that you are constantly surrounded by angels executing Allah's will? If you truly believed that angels are powerful and all around you, would you still sin privately? Would you speak differently? Act differently? Make a firm intention today to live with the consciousness that the angels are watching.
?
Every time you recite the Quran, remember: These very words were brought down by a mighty angel, Gabriel, to the heart of Prophet Muhammad. The chain from Allah to you involves a being of immense strength and honor. Now ask yourself: Have I ever read the Quran with this awe-inspiring awareness? Or have I taken the words for granted? Will you commit to reciting even one verse today with the deep sense that it is a message delivered by a noble messenger straight from your Lord?

The Circularity Argument Regarding Angelic Infallibility
Author argues that angelic infallibility is needed for miracles to prove prophethood, but it can only be known through revelation, creating circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity problem that arises when trying to prove prophethood through miracles without prior knowledge of angelic infallibility.

Core Idea
Proving prophethood via miracles requires prior knowledge of angelic infallibility, leading to a vicious circle.

Having established the Quranic basis for angels, the author now presents a logical problem. If we do not already know that angels are infallible, miracles could be attributed to them, undermining their evidential value for prophethood. But knowledge of angelic infallibility comes only from revelation, which itself depends on prophethood. This creates a circular dependency that must be resolved. The author states the circle is invalid, setting up the need for an alternative foundation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional
Read the passage starting from 'إذا عرفت هذا فنقول'. Notice the conditional: if we do not know angels are infallible, miracles could be performed by them.
This shifts from Quranic evidence to a logical conditional.
2
Trace the circular dependency
Identify the chain: knowledge of angelic infallibility depends on transmitted proofs, which depend on truthfulness of messengers, which depends on miracles, which depend on angelic infallibility. Follow each step.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that this is a circle and a circle is invalid. Think about why that matters for proving prophethood.
This argument shows that relying solely on miracles to prove prophethood requires an assumption that is itself not proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Is it based on miracles you've heard about, or on something deeper—perhaps a direct conviction from Allah? What would it mean for your faith if the arguments for it were circular?
?

How does that feel—is it unsettling or freeing? Ask yourself: Are you willing to let go of the need to rationally prove everything in your deen, trusting Allah's words over your own intellect?
