The First Objection: Uncertainty of Miracle's Origin
First objection: Ambiguous origin of miracles due to good and evil spirits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against miracles as proof of prophethood: the ambiguity of whether a miracle comes from a good or evil spiritual source.

Core Idea
Miracles could be from Iblis as easily as from pure spirits — so how can we trust them?

This lesson introduces the first of two objections that challenge the evidentiary value of miracles. The objection points to the universal agreement on the existence of both malevolent and benevolent spiritual beings. When a miracle occurs, it is impossible to know which side is acting, undermining the miracle as a clear sign from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the first objection passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation for the first objection. Notice it begins with 'الاول' and ends at the question about Iblis.
The objection is framed as an agreed-upon fact about two kinds of spirits.
2
Identify the problem
The objection claims that because both good and evil spirits exist, a miracle could be from either. This creates uncertainty about the miracle's divine origin.
The key phrase is 'فكيف يعرف أنه من إعانة الأرواح الطاهرة... وليس من إعانة ذلك الروح المفسد'
3
Reflect on the challenge
Consider why this is a serious challenge to using miracles as proof. If the source is ambiguous, the miracle loses its evidentiary value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يقرر هذا السؤال وجهان: الأول: إن الناس اتفقوا على وجود شيء قادر قاهر مسئول على هذا العالم، وهو المسمى: إبليس، وأنه لا يدعو إلا إلى الأباطيل والكفر، واتفقوا أيضاً على وجود شيء قادر قاهر يدعو إلى الخير والصلاح والدين. فإذا ظهر على يد الرسول هذا المعجز، فكيف يعرف أنه من إعانة الأرواح الطاهرة المطيعة، وليس من إعانة ذلك الروح المفسد المؤذي؟ والوجه الثاني: إنا نورد هذا السؤال على عبارات الصائبة والفلاسفة. وذلك لأن الكل اتفقوا على إثبات الأرواح الفلكية، وأن لكل واحد منها نوعاً آخر من التأثيرات في هذا العالم. والشرائع أيضاً ناطقة بذلك. فإنهم أثبتوا ملكاً هو ملك الجبال، وملكاً آخر، هو ملك البحار، وملكاً ثالثاً، هو ملك الأمطار، ورابعاً هو ملك الأرزاق، وخامساً هو ملك الموت، وسادساً هو ملك الحرب والقتل. والهند اتفقوا على ذلك، على ما شرحنا مذاهبهم في هذا الباب. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فلم لا يجوز أن تكون هذه المعجزات من أفعال هذه الأرواح؟ بل نقول: إن هذا القول هو القول المتفق عليه بين الصائبة والفلاسفة، وأهل الهند وأصحاب الطلسمات. وإذا كان هذا قولاً متفقاً عليه بين هذه الفرق فما لم تذكروا في إبطاله دليلاً، لم يحصل المقصود البتة.
And what confirms this question are two aspects: The first: People have agreed upon the existence of something powerful and overwhelming that is responsible for this world, named Iblis, and that he only calls to falsehoods and disbelief. And they also agreed upon the existence of something powerful and overwhelming that calls to goodness, righteousness, and religion. So when this miracle appears by the hand of the messenger, how can it be known that it is from the assistance of the pure obedient spirits and not from the assistance of that corrupt harmful spirit? The second aspect: We present this question according to the statements of the Sabians and philosophers. That is because all have agreed on the affirmation of the celestial spirits, and that each one of them has another type of influence in this world. And the religious laws also speak of that. For they affirmed an angel who is the angel of mountains, another angel of seas, a third angel of rain, a fourth angel of provisions, a fifth angel of death, and a sixth angel of war and killing. And the Hindus agreed on that, as we have explained their doctrines in this chapter. If that is the case, then why is it not possible that these miracles are from the actions of these spirits? Rather we say: This statement is the agreed-upon statement among the Sabians, philosophers, the people of India, and the practitioners of talismans. And if this is an agreed-upon statement among these groups, then as long as you do not mention a proof to invalidate it, the desired end is not achieved at all.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct objections against the use of miracles as proof of prophethood. The first objection appeals to common agreement on the existence of both good and evil spiritual forces (Iblis and pure spirits). When a miracle occurs, it could be from either source, so one cannot be certain it is from a divine agent supporting the prophet. The second objection draws on Sabian and philosophical doctrines of celestial spirits, each with specific influences, and notes that even religious texts affirm various angels for natural phenomena. Since many groups agree that such spirits can produce effects, miracles could be attributed to these spirits rather than to God. The author concludes that until a proof is given to rule out these possibilities, the argument from miracles is inconclusive.

Key Terms
إبليس
أرواح طاهرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the author is endorsing that miracles are always from Iblis.
Correction: The author is presenting an objection that needs to be answered, not stating his own belief.

Checkpoint
According to the first objection, why is it difficult to determine the source of a miracle?
A) Because miracles are impossible.
B) Because both good and evil spirits can perform them.
C) Because people disagree on whether Iblis exists.
D) Because miracles are only illusions.

Key Takeaway
The first objection argues that miracles are ambiguous because they could be from either good or evil spiritual sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says Iblis 'only calls to falsehoods and disbelief.' In the quiet moments of your day, what falsehoods are you allowing to enter your heart? How can you actively counter them with truth from the Qur'an and Sunnah this week?
?
When you experience something that seems miraculous or divinely guided, how do you test its source? Do you immediately attribute it to Allah, or do you sometimes doubt? What criteria from this lesson can help you discern?
?
The objection highlights that both good and evil spirits can produce powerful events. In your own life, have you ever been deceived by something that seemed good but led you away from the straight path? How can you commit to seeking Allah's protection from such deception?

The Second Objection: Celestial Spirits as Alternative Explanations
Second objection: Celestial spirits as possible causes of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection that miracles could be attributed to celestial spirits, as affirmed by Sabians, philosophers, Hindus, and even religious texts.

Core Idea
Many traditions believe celestial spirits control natural phenomena — so miracles could be their work.

The second objection draws on widespread beliefs in celestial spirits (أرواح فلكية) that have specific influences in the world. Both religious laws and various groups like the Sabians and philosophers affirm these spirits. Therefore, miracles could be explained as actions of these spirits rather than divine intervention. Until this possibility is ruled out, the argument from miracles remains inconclusive.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second objection. Note how it begins with 'والوجه الثاني' and lists various spirits and groups.
It mentions angels of mountains, seas, rain, etc., as examples.
2
Identify the types of spirits mentioned
The passage refers to celestial spirits (أرواح فلكية) and gives specific examples of angels from religious texts: angel of mountains, angel of seas, etc.
Also mentions Hindus and practitioners of talismans.
3
Understand the objection's force
The objection argues that since many groups agree that these spirits can influence the world, miracles could be their actions. Thus, without a proof to rule this out, the miracle's divine origin is not certain.
The conclusion: 'فما لم تذكروا في إبطاله دليلاً، لم يحصل المقصود البتة.'

And they also agreed upon the existence of something powerful and overwhelming that calls to goodness, righteousness, and religion. The first objection appeals to common agreement on the existence of both good and evil spiritual forces (Iblis and pure spirits). When a miracle occurs, it could be from either source, so one cannot be certain it is from a divine agent supporting the prophet. The second objection draws on Sabian and philosophical doctrines of celestial spirits, each with specific influences, and notes that even religious texts affirm various angels for natural phenomena. Since many groups agree that such spirits can produce effects, miracles could be attributed to these spirits rather than to God. The author concludes that until a proof is given to rule out these possibilities, the argument from miracles is inconclusive.

Key Terms
أرواح فلكية
صابئة
فلاسفة
طلسمات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author accepts the objection as valid and thus rejects prophethood.
Correction: The author is presenting challenges that must be addressed; he does not endorse them.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, what is a possible explanation for miracles besides divine action?
A) They are illusions created by false prophets.
B) They are the actions of celestial spirits.
C) They are natural coincidences.
D) They are caused by human effort.

Key Takeaway
The second objection holds that miracles could be attributed to celestial spirits, a view shared by multiple traditions, undermining the certainty of divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objection suggests that miracles attributed to prophets could be explained by spirits. In your own life, are there experiences you attribute to chance, fate, or hidden forces that you should instead recognize as from Allah? What would it take for you to shift that perspective?
?
The passage shows that many groups agree on spirits but disagree on their source. How often do you accept a claim just because many people believe it? Pledge to examine one belief you hold based on popular consensus and seek its proof from revelation.
?
This lesson demands a proof to refute an argument. What is one area of your faith where you have accepted something without seeking evidence? Commit to finding a proof from the Quran or Sunnah for that belief this week.

The Circularity Objection and Two Arguments Against Miracles as Proof
Objector presents circularity and two arguments against miracles as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how objectors use the circularity problem and the existence of multiple powerful spirits to challenge the evidential value of miracles in proving prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles alone cannot prove prophethood unless we can rule out other spiritual sources.

Before we can affirm that miracles are reliable signs of prophethood, we must confront objections from skeptics who propose alternative explanations. This passage presents a sophisticated objection: it first points out a logical circularity, then offers two specific arguments showing that miracles could be attributed to other spirits—evil ones or celestial spirits—thereby undermining their exclusive connection to divine truth.

Guided Path
1
Understand the circularity objection
Read the opening lines: the objector says knowledge of messengers' truthfulness depends on angelic infallibility, but that itself depends on the messengers. This is a circle, and circles are invalid.
Notice the objector is using this to question the whole framework.
2
Examine the first aspect
Focus on the first argument: people agree on the existence of both Iblis (evil spirit) and a good spirit. A miracle could come from either, so how can we know which one assisted the messenger?
This challenges the assumption that miracles are always from good spirits.
3
Examine the second aspect
Read the second argument: Sabians, philosophers, and Indians affirm multiple celestial spirits (kings of mountains, seas, etc.) that influence the world. Miracles could be their acts, not divine signs.
This broadens the objection to include various religious traditions.
4
Recognize the objector's conclusion
The objector ends by saying that since these views are widely accepted, the proponent must provide a proof to refute them, otherwise the miracle's value remains unproven.
This sets up the need for a response in subsequent lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسالة. والعلم بصدقهم يتوقف على عصمة الملائكة، وذلك دور، والدور باطل. والذي يقرر هذا السؤال وجهان: الأول: إن الناس اتفقوا على وجود شيء قادر قاهر مسئول على هذا العالم، وهو المسمى: إبليس، وأنه لا يدعو إلا إلى الأباطيل والكفر، واتفقوا أيضاً على وجود شيء قادر قاهر يدعو إلى الخير والصلاح والدين. فإذا ظهر على يد الرسول هذا المعجز، فكيف يعرف أنه من إعانة الأرواح الطاهرة المطيعة، وليس من إعانة ذلك الروح المفسد المؤذي؟ والوجه الثاني: إنا نورد هذا السؤال على عبارات الصائبة والفلاسفة. وذلك لأن الكل اتفقوا على إثبات الأرواح الفلكية، واتفقوا عليها أن لكل واحد منها نوعاً آخر من التأثيرات في هذا العالم، والشرائع أيضاً ناطقة بذلك. فإنهم أثبتوا ملكاً هو ملك الجبال، وملكاً آخر هو ملك البحار، وملكاً ثالثاً هو ملك الأمطار، ورابعاً هو ملك الأرزاق، وخامساً هو ملك الموت، وسادساً هو ملك الحرب والقتل. والهند اتفقوا على ذلك، على ما شرحنا مذاهبهم في هذا الباب. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فلم لا يجوز أن تكون هذه المعجزات من أفعال هذه الأرواح؟ بل نقول: إن هذا القول هو القول المتفق عليه بين الصائبة والفلاسفة، وأهل الهند وأصحاب الطلسمات. وإذا كان هذا قولاً متفقاً عليه بين هذه الفرق فما لم تذكروا في إبطاله دليلاً، لم يحصل المقصود البتة.
The message? And the knowledge of their truthfulness depends on the infallibility of the angels, and that is a circle, and the circle is false. And the one who formulates this question has two aspects: First: that people have agreed upon the existence of a powerful, overwhelming entity that has control over this world, and it is named Iblis, and that he does not call except to falsehoods and disbelief, and they also agreed upon the existence of a powerful, overwhelming entity that calls to good, righteousness, and religion. So when this miracle appears at the hand of the messenger, how is it known that it is from the assistance of the pure, obedient spirits and not from the assistance of that corrupting, harmful spirit? And the second aspect: we pose this question to the statements of the Sabians and philosophers. That is because everyone agreed on affirming the celestial spirits, and they agreed upon them that each one of them has another type of influences in this world, and the divine laws also speak of that. For they affirmed a king who is the king of mountains, and another king who is the king of seas, and a third king who is the king of rains, and a fourth who is the king of provisions, and a fifth who is the king of death, and a sixth who is the king of war and killing. And the Indians agreed upon that, as we have explained their doctrines in this chapter. And if the matter is so, then why is it not permissible that these miracles are from the acts of these spirits? Rather we say: This statement is the statement agreed upon by the Sabians, the philosophers, the people of India, and the masters of talismans. And if this is a statement agreed upon among these sects, then as long as you have not mentioned a proof to refute it, the objective is not attained at all.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the evidential value of miracles. It begins by noting a circularity: knowledge of the messengers' truthfulness depends on the infallibility of angels (who bring revelation), but knowledge of angelic infallibility depends on the truthfulness of the messengers. This circle is invalid. Then the objector offers two aspects (arguments) to press the objection. The first aspect appeals to universal agreement that there are two powerful spiritual forces: Iblis (evil) and a good spirit. When a miracle occurs, how can we tell it comes from the good spirit rather than the evil one? The second aspect appeals to the doctrines of Sabians, philosophers, and Indians, who affirm multiple celestial spirits (kings of mountains, seas, etc.) and argue that miracles could be acts of these spirits. Since these views are widespread, the objector demands a proof to refute them before the miracle can be accepted as a divine sign.

Key Terms
عصمة الملائكة
دور
إبليس
أرواح فلكية
صائبة
طلسمات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the author is affirming the reality of Iblis and celestial spirits as valid explanations of miracles.
Correction: The author is merely presenting an objection that must be refuted; the author does not endorse these views.

Checkpoint
According to the first aspect of the objection, why is it difficult to know that a miracle comes from a good spirit?
A) Because miracles are not real.
B) Because both Iblis and good spirits can perform miracles, and we cannot distinguish which one produced it.
C) Because the miracle itself is ambiguous.
D) Because angels are not trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The objection argues that miracles cannot uniquely prove prophethood because they could be attributed to other spirits—either evil or celestial—and a circularity undermines the foundational assumption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something you consider a sign from God, how do you know it is truly from Him and not from another source? What would it take for you to doubt your own certainty?
?
The objection challenges the evidentiary value of miracles by pointing to alternatives. Are there beliefs you hold that you have never critically examined for possible alternative explanations? What would it cost you to examine them now?
?
If you were asked to provide a proof that a particular miracle could only come from God, how would you begin? What does that reveal about the strength of your own faith?

The Astrologers' Claims on Conjunctions and Lots
The author enumerates the astrologers' agreed-upon claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key astrological claims that some use to explain miracles.

Core Idea
Astrologers claim planetary conjunctions and lots can produce extraordinary events.

Before refuting the astrological objection, the author presents the precise claims of astrologers. These include the influence of planetary conjunctions, the lot of fortune, and the lot of the unseen. The author is not endorsing these views but setting them up for his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the astrologers' claims
Read the first paragraph of the passage carefully. Note the three agreements that astrologers have made across time.
The author uses the word 'agreed' repeatedly to show consensus.
2
Identify the three main claims
Identify the three specific claims: (1) conjunctions have effects, (2) states of conjunctions depend on fixed stars in appropriate houses, (3) the lot of fortune and lot of the unseen have specific effects.
The lot of fortune is associated with fortunes, the lot of the unseen with knowledge of the hidden.
3
Note the astrologers' certainty
Observe that the author reports astrologers insist on these claims and claim certainty from experience.
This sets up the contrast with the author's own position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واتفقوا أيضاً على أن للقرانات آثاراً عظيمة في هذا الباب. واتفقوا على أنه لا تختلف أحوال تلك القرانات إلا وقوع الثوابت في البيوت المناسبة لها. واتفقوا على أن لسهم السعادة تأثيراً قوياً في إعطاء السعادات، ولسهم الغيب تأثيراً قوياً في إعطاء المعارف الحقة والوقوف على المغيبات. وعلماء الأحكام من الزمان الأقدم إلى عهدنا هذا مصرون على صحة هذه الدعاوى، وجازمون بأن كل من جرب أحوال الطوالع علم يقينا أن لهذه الأسباب آثاراً قوية في هذا الباب.

إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: نحن لا ندعي صحة هذه الأصول، ولا أنها معلومة أو مظنونة، بل نقول: لا أقل من أن يكون احتمال أن يكون الأمر على ما قالوه قائماً. وبتقدير أن تصح كل هذه الأشياء أو بعضها، أن يكون اختصاص مدعي النبوة والرسالة بهذه المعجزات إنما كان لأجل اشتمال طالع مولده على حالة من هذه الأحوال. فلعله وقع سهم السعادة وقوعاً عجيباً يقتضي حصول هذه السعادات. ولعله وقع سهم الغيب في طالعه وقوعاً يقتضي قدرته على الإخبار عن الغيوب.

وأنا أقول: إني قد رأيت إنساناً لم يتفق في طالع مولده شيء من الأشياء الكاملة، إلا أنه كانت الشعري اليمانية واقعة على درجة تاسعة. فلا جرم بلغ في العلوم النقلية والعقلية مبلغاً عالياً، من غير حاجة إلى تحمل تعب في المطالعة والتحصيل.

وإذا ثبت أن هذا الاحتمال قائم، ظهر أنه لا سبيل البتة إلى القطع بأن هذه الخوارق التي ظهرت على الأنبياء من فعل الله تعالى.

وحكى محمد بن زكريا الرازي في بعض كتبه: أنه رأى رجلاً يهودياً، كان يستخرج الخبيء والضمير على أحسن الوجوه، وبقي على تلك الحالة سنين. ثم زالت عنه تلك الحالة. قال: فأخبرني جماعة من المنجمين: أن الجان يخبر ذلك الرجل لأنه وقع في قسمه ما يوجب التكهن. فلما زالت تلك القسيمة، زالت تلك الصفة عن ذلك الرجل.
And they also agreed that conjunctions have great effects in this matter. And they agreed that the states of those conjunctions do not differ except by the occurrence of the fixed stars in houses appropriate to them. And they agreed that the lot of fortune has a strong effect in granting fortunes, and the lot of the unseen has a strong effect in granting true knowledge and awareness of hidden things. And the astrologers from the earliest times until our present day insist on the correctness of these claims, and are certain that everyone who has experimented with the states of nativities knows with certainty that these causes have strong effects in this matter.

When you know this, we say: We do not claim the correctness of these foundations, nor that they are known or presumed, but we say: At the very least, there is a possibility that the matter is as they said. And assuming that all these things or some of them are correct, then the distinction of the claimant of prophethood and messengers with these miracles was only due to the inclusion in the ascendant of his birth of a state from among these states. So perhaps the lot of fortune fell in a wondrous way requiring the attainment of these fortunes. And perhaps the lot of the unseen fell in his ascendant in a way requiring his ability to inform about hidden things.

And I say: I have seen a person whose birth ascendant did not contain any of the perfect things, except that Sirius of Yemen was falling on the ninth degree. So inevitably he reached a high level in the transmitted and rational sciences, without needing to endure exertion in reading and study.

And if it is established that this possibility exists, it becomes clear that there is no way at all to be certain that these extraordinary events that appeared from the prophets are from the act of God Almighty.

And Muhammad ibn Zakariyya al-Razi narrated in some of his books that he saw a Jewish man who used to extract what was hidden and the inner conscience in the best ways, and he remained in that state for years. Then that state left him. He said: So a group of astrologers informed me that the jinn were informing that man because he had in his lot what required divination. When that lot left, that quality left that man.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth probability that could explain the miracles of prophets without attributing them directly to God. It first summarizes the claims of astrologers about the effects of planetary conjunctions, the lot of fortune, and the lot of the unseen. Then the author states that even if these astrological claims are not proven, they constitute a possibility that prevents certainty that miracles are solely from God. He supports this with a personal observation of a man who achieved great knowledge due to a stellar configuration, and with an anecdote from al-Razi about a Jewish man whose ability to know hidden things was attributed to astrological influences. The argument is that as long as such possibilities exist, one cannot be certain that the miracles of prophets are exclusively from God.

سهم الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: The author accepts these astrological claims as true.
Correction: The author does not claim correctness; he presents them as a possible objection to prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do astrologers agree about the lot of the unseen?
A) It has no effect on knowledge.
B) It has a strong effect in granting true knowledge and awareness of hidden things.
C) It only affects fortunes.
D) It is unrelated to conjunctions.

Key Takeaway
Astrologers claim that planetary conjunctions and lots have strong effects on extraordinary events, which forms the basis of the objection to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever checked your horoscope or felt that the position of stars might influence your luck or future? This passage reveals that such claims are mere assertions from astrologers. In your heart, do you truly rely on Allah alone for your fortune and knowledge of the unseen, or is there a hint of belief in these things? Make a firm resolve today to purge any such thoughts and affirm that only Allah knows the unseen and controls all affairs.
?
If someone told you that planetary conjunctions cause disasters or good fortune, would you be swayed? This lesson shows that astrologers insist on these claims, but they offer no proof from revelation. Ask yourself: Are there any areas in your life where you give more weight to superstitious beliefs or worldly patterns than to the Qur'an and Sunnah? Commit to seeking knowledge of true tawheed to guard your heart.
?
How would you feel if a close friend followed astrology religiously? This passage can help you see that such beliefs are based on accumulation of claims, not truth. But first, examine your own heart: Do you ever rely on 'good luck charms', certain days, or numbers? This lesson calls you to abandon all false causes and submit solely to Allah's decree. What step will you take today to strengthen your tawheed?

The Possibility That Astrology Explains Miracles
The author presents the possibility argument and its conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mere possibility of astrological influence prevents certainty about the divine origin of miracles.

Core Idea
Even if astrology is unproven, its possibility blocks certainty.

The author now makes his crucial move. He does not need to prove astrology true; he only needs to show that it could be true. This possibility, however remote, is enough to challenge the absolute certainty that miracles come exclusively from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the second paragraph of the passage. Note the author's initial disclaimer and the conditional structure.
The author says 'we do not claim correctness'—this is key.
2
Identify the logical structure
The argument is: (a) There is at least a possibility that astrological claims are true. (b) If those claims are true, then miracles could be caused by astrology. (c) Therefore, we cannot be certain that miracles are from God alone.
The conclusion is that certainty is impossible if this possibility exists.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that the author is not denying miracles are from God; he is arguing that the astrological objection raises a doubt that prevents absolute certainty.
This is a common apologetic strategy: showing that opposing views cannot be definitively ruled out.

Anecdotal Support for Astrological Explanations
The author provides two anecdotes as evidence of astrological effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will examine the anecdotal evidence the author presents to illustrate the possibility of astrological influence on extraordinary abilities.

Core Idea
The author uses anecdotes to show that astrological influences could explain knowledge and divination.

To reinforce that astrological influence is not just theoretical, the author shares two anecdotes: one from his own experience of a scholar whose achievement was linked to a stellar configuration, and another from al-Razi about a Jewish man whose ability to know hidden things was tied to astrological lots. These stories serve as concrete examples of how extraordinary abilities might arise from astronomical causes.

Guided Path
1
Read the personal observation
Read the third paragraph where the author shares his own experience. Note the specific stellar configuration mentioned (Sirius at the ninth degree) and the outcome.
The author implies this configuration replaced the need for hard study.
2
Read the anecdote from al-Razi
Read the fourth paragraph about the Jewish man. Note that the man's ability to know hidden things was attributed to astrological lots and jinn communication.
The ability left when the astrological lot changed.
3
Connect to the argument
Understand that these anecdotes are meant to show that such possibilities are not abstract—they have been observed. This strengthens the argument that we cannot dismiss astrology as a possible explanation for miracles.
The author does not claim these prove astrology, but they illustrate that the possibility exists in reality.

واتفقوا أيضاً على أن للقرانات آثاراً عظيمة في هذا الباب. واتفقوا على أنه لا تختلف أحوال تلك القرانات إلا وقوع الثوابت في البيوت المناسبة لها. واتفقوا على أن لسهم السعادة تأثيراً قوياً في إعطاء السعادات، ولسهم الغيب تأثيراً قوياً في إعطاء المعارف الحقة والوقوف على المغيبات. وعلماء الأحكام من الزمان الأقدم إلى عهدنا هذا مصرون على صحة هذه الدعاوى، وجازمون بأن كل من جرب أحوال الطوالع علم يقينا أن لهذه الأسباب آثاراً قوية في هذا الباب.

إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: نحن لا ندعي صحة هذه الأصول، ولا أنها معلومة أو مظنونة، بل نقول: لا أقل من أن يكون احتمال أن يكون الأمر على ما قالوه قائماً. وبتقدير أن تصح كل هذه الأشياء أو بعضها، أن يكون اختصاص مدعي النبوة والرسالة بهذه المعجزات إنما كان لأجل اشتمال طالع مولده على حالة من هذه الأحوال. فلعله وقع سهم السعادة وقوعاً عجيباً يقتضي حصول هذه السعادات. ولعله وقع سهم الغيب في طالعه وقوعاً يقتضي قدرته على الإخبار عن الغيوب.

وأنا أقول: إني قد رأيت إنساناً لم يتفق في طالع مولده شيء من الأشياء الكاملة، إلا أنه كانت الشعري اليمانية واقعة على درجة تاسعة. فلا جرم بلغ في العلوم النقلية والعقلية مبلغاً عالياً، من غير حاجة إلى تحمل تعب في المطالعة والتحصيل.

وإذا ثبت أن هذا الاحتمال قائم، ظهر أنه لا سبيل البتة إلى القطع بأن هذه الخوارق التي ظهرت على الأنبياء من فعل الله تعالى.

وحكى محمد بن زكريا الرازي في بعض كتبه: أنه رأى رجلاً يهودياً، كان يستخرج الخبيء والضمير على أحسن الوجوه، وبقي على تلك الحالة سنين. ثم زالت عنه تلك الحالة. قال: فأخبرني جماعة من المنجمين: أن الجان يخبر ذلك الرجل لأنه وقع في قسمه ما يوجب التكهن. فلما زالت تلك القسيمة، زالت تلك الصفة عن ذلك الرجل.
And they also agreed that conjunctions have great effects in this matter. And they agreed that the states of those conjunctions do not differ except by the occurrence of the fixed stars in houses appropriate to them. And they agreed that the lot of fortune has a strong effect in granting fortunes, and the lot of the unseen has a strong effect in granting true knowledge and awareness of hidden things. And the astrologers from the earliest times until our present day insist on the correctness of these claims, and are certain that everyone who has experimented with the states of nativities knows with certainty that these causes have strong effects in this matter.

When you know this, we say: We do not claim the correctness of these foundations, nor that they are known or presumed, but we say: At the very least, there is a possibility that the matter is as they said. And assuming that all these things or some of them are correct, then the distinction of the claimant of prophethood and messengers with these miracles was only due to the inclusion in the ascendant of his birth of a state from among these states. So perhaps the lot of fortune fell in a wondrous way requiring the attainment of these fortunes. And perhaps the lot of the unseen fell in his ascendant in a way requiring his ability to inform about hidden things.

And I say: I have seen a person whose birth ascendant did not contain any of the perfect things, except that Sirius of Yemen was falling on the ninth degree. So inevitably he reached a high level in the transmitted and rational sciences, without needing to endure exertion in reading and study.

And if it is established that this possibility exists, it becomes clear that there is no way at all to be certain that these extraordinary events that appeared from the prophets are from the act of God Almighty.

And Muhammad ibn Zakariyya al-Razi narrated in some of his books that he saw a Jewish man who used to extract what was hidden and the inner conscience in the best ways, and he remained in that state for years. Then that state left him. He said: So a group of astrologers informed me that the jinn were informing that man because he had in his lot what required divination. When that lot left, that quality left that man.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth probability that could explain the miracles of prophets without attributing them directly to God. It first summarizes the claims of astrologers about the effects of planetary conjunctions, the lot of fortune, and the lot of the unseen. Then the author states that even if these astrological claims are not proven, they constitute a possibility that prevents certainty that miracles are solely from God. He supports this with a personal observation of a man who achieved great knowledge due to a stellar configuration, and with an anecdote from al-Razi about a Jewish man whose ability to know hidden things was attributed to astrological influences. The argument is that as long as such possibilities exist, one cannot be certain that the miracles of prophets are exclusively from God.

Magic and Celestial Spirits: The Sixth Probability
Author presents magical/spirit objection and distinguishes from astrological one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the magical/celestial spirits objection challenges the certainty of divine miracles and how it differs from the astrological causal model.

Core Idea
Possibility alone suffices to undermine certainty unless impossibility is proven.

The author continues his series of alternative explanations for miracles by presenting a view attributed to philosophers and Sabians: that celestial beings are living, rational, and can be invoked through magical rites. While he does not endorse this view, he uses it to show that the claim of divine miracles cannot be certain as long as even a mere possibility exists. This lesson explores that objection and the key distinction between this and the previous astrological one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, then a response, then a distinction.
The author uses the phrase 'إذا عرفت هذا الكلام فنقول' to transition to his response.
2
Identify the core claim and the author's response
Find where the author states the Sabian/philosopher claim about celestial spirits, and then where he presents his argument that even unproven possibility prevents certainty.
3
Distinguish the two objections
The author explicitly distinguishes this objection from the previous one. Understand the difference: in the previous, planets are direct causes; here, spirits are invoked through magic.
This distinction is crucial for the overall argument.
4
Reflect on the burden of proof
Notice that the author shifts the burden: the questioner does not need to prove the objection, only the responder must prove impossibility.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاحتمال السادس: اتفقت الفلاسفة والصائبة على أن الأفلاك والكواكب أحياء ناطقة، مطلعة على جميع أحوال هذا العالم. وفي الناس من يدعي: أن الرجل إذا واظب على قراءة رقي مخصوصة أياماً مخصوصة على شرائط مخصوصة، فإنه يتجلى له روح ذلك الكوكب، ويعينه على مقاصده وأغراضه. وكتب أصحاب الطلسمات في دعوة الكواكب مملوءة من هذه الكلمات.

إذا عرفت هذا الكلام فنقول: إنه وإن لم يثبت بالدليل صحة ما ذكروه، إلا أنه لا أقل من الاحتمال. ومع قيام هذا الاحتمال، لا يمكن القطع بأن خالق المعجزات هو الله تعالى. بل لا يمتنع أن يكون فاعلها هو هذه الكواكب، ومن نظر في كتب السحر والطلمسات، رأى حكايات عجيبة في هذا الباب. وكتاب تنكلوشا كتاب مشهور، موجود في أيدي الناس، وفيه من هذا الباب شيء كثير، وقول من يقول: إنه من باب الخرافات كلام ما به بأس، إلا أنه لا يدفع السؤال. لأن السائل لا حاجة به إلى إقامة الدليل على صحة ما ذكره في السؤال. وإنما المجيب هو المحتاج إلى إقامة الدلالة على أن ذلك الوجه محال باطل قطعاً.

واعلم أن الفرق بين هذا السؤال، وبين ما قبله: أما في السؤال الأول جعلنا الكواكب موجبة بالذات، لهذه الآثار العجيبة، بحسب الشرائط المختلفة، والأشكال الفلكية المتعاقبة.
The sixth probability: The philosophers and Sabians agreed that the celestial spheres and planets are living, rational beings, informed of all conditions of this world. And among people there are those who claim that if a person persists in reciting specific spells on specific days under specific conditions, then the spirit of that planet becomes manifest to him and helps him in his objectives and purposes. And the books of the talismanists concerning the invocation of planets are filled with these words.

When you know this speech, we say: Even if the correctness of what they mentioned is not proven by evidence, yet at the very least there is possibility. And given this possibility, it is not possible to be certain that the creator of miracles is God Almighty. Rather, it is not impossible that the doer of them is these planets. And whoever looks into the books of magic and talismans sees amazing stories in this matter. And the book Tinkalusha is a well-known book, existing in people's hands, and in it is much of this matter. And the statement of whoever says that it is from the realm of superstitions is a statement that is fine, except that it does not repel the objection. Because the questioner has no need to produce evidence for the correctness of what he mentioned in the question. Rather, the responder is the one in need of producing evidence that that way is absolutely impossible and false.

And know that the difference between this objection and the one before it: In the first objection, we made the planets cause in themselves for these wondrous effects, according to different conditions and successive celestial configurations.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth probability that miracles might be caused by the spirits of planets invoked through magical practices. The author first states the claim of philosophers and Sabians that celestial bodies are living, rational, and aware of all worldly affairs. Then he notes that some people claim that by reciting specific spells under specific conditions, the spirit of a planet appears and aids the person. The author then argues that even if these claims are not proven, the mere possibility prevents certainty that miracles are from God. He mentions the book Tinkalusha as an example of such magical literature. Finally, he distinguishes this objection from the previous one: in the astrological objection (the fifth probability), the planets were considered as direct causes by themselves according to configurations; here, the planets are invoked through magic, and the spirits act as agents.

The possibility of magical celestial causation, even if unproven, undermines the certainty that miracles come only from God unless impossibility is demonstrated.

The Seventh Possibility: Intellects and Souls as Miracles' Agents
Al-Razi presents the seventh possibility: separate intellects and souls as miracle agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's objection that if philosophers are right about separate intellects and souls, those could be the agents of miracles, undermining the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
If intellects and souls exist, they could cause miracles, not prophets.

Al-Razi continues his critique of the standard evidence for prophethood. He introduces a possibility drawn from the philosophers: if separate intellects and souls exist independently, they might be the true agents of miraculous events. This lesson examines that challenge and its implications for the theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the seventh possibility passage
Read the Arabic passage for the seventh possibility and its translation. Notice how al-Razi frames this as a distinct objection from the angel question.
He distinguishes between angels (accepted by theologians) and intellects/souls (accepted by philosophers).
2
Understand the core argument
Al-Razi argues that if the philosophers' claim is true (that intellects and souls exist and act), then miracles could be attributed to them rather than to a prophet's divine connection.
3
Compare with the angel objection
Al-Razi clarifies that the angel objection (earlier) is based on theologians' beliefs, while this one is based on philosophical doctrines. This shows his method of addressing multiple schools.
4
Reflect on the evidential impact
Ask yourself: if this possibility is not ruled out, how does it weaken the claim that miracles prove prophethood?
The miracle's agent becomes ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في هذا السؤال . فقد جعلنا الأفلاك والكواكب ، أحياء ناطقة .. مختارة في الفعل والترك
والاحتمال السابع : اتفقت الفلاسفة على إثبات العقول والنفوس . فقبل إقامة الدلالة على إبطال القول بها ، كان احتمال وجودها قائماً . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون فاعل هذه المعجزات هو هذه العقول والنفوس ؟ والفرق بين هذا السؤال وبين سؤال الملائكة : هو أن الملائكة عند المتكلمين شيء مغاير لهذه العقول والنفوس ، فأوردنا سؤال الملائكة على حسب ما يعتقدون في وجود الملائكة ، وأوردنا هذا السؤال ههنا على حسب مذاهب الفلاسفة في العقول والنفوس
·
الاحتمال الثامن : أن نقول : لا شك أن أجسام هذا العالم العنصري ، مشتركة في الهيولى. وتلك الهيولى قابلة لجميع الصور والأعراض على البدن وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : اختصاص كل واحد من هذه الأجسام بصفته المعينة وصورته المعينة ، إما أن يكون لأجل أن ذلك الجسم كان أولى بقبول تلك الصفة والصورة من سائر الأجسام أو لم يكن كذلك . والثاني باطل . وإلا لزم أن يكون اختصاص ذلك الجسم بتلك الصفة مع كونه مساوياً لسائر الأجسام في القبول ، وفي عدم الأولوية ، يكون رجحانا ، لأحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر ، لا لمرجح ، وهو محال . ولما بطل هذا القسم ، ثبت أن القسم الأول حق . فنقول : واختصاص ذلك الجسم بذلك الاستعداد الخاص ، لا بد وأن يكون لأجل استعداد آخر ؛ إلى غير النهاية ، فتلك الاستعدادات إن حصلت دفعة واحدة ، لزم حصول أسباب ومسببات لا نهاية لها ، دفعة واحدة . وهو محال ، وإن حصلت على سبيل التعاقب ، وهو أن يكون كل استعداد سابق ، علة الحصول الاستعداد اللاحق ، فحينئذ يكون حصول هذا المعجز المعين الذي هو فعل خارق للعادة من لوازم الأحوال السالفة ، التي لا أول لها . وحينئذ تخرج عن كونها دالة على الصدق
·
والحاصل : أنه إن كان ذلك الجسم مساوياً ، لسائر الأجسام ، وكان ذلك الوقت مساوياً لسائر الأوقات، في قبول ذلك الحادث المعين ، فحينئذ قد ترجح الممكن لا المرجح . وإذا جاز هذا ، فلم لا يجوز حدوث المعجز ، لا لغرض أصلاً ؟ وذلك يبطل القول بدلالة المعجز على الصدق .
وأيضاً : إما أن يتوقف حدوث ذلك الحادث على كون ذلك الجسم موصوفاً بذلك الاستعداد الخاص ، فحينئذ يكون حدوث هذا المعجز من لوازم الأحوال السالفة . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فإنه يخرج عن كونه دليلا على صدق المدعي
As for this question, we have made the celestial spheres and planets, living rational beings... free will in action and omission. The seventh possibility: The philosophers agreed on affirming intellects and souls. So before establishing the proof for invalidating the claim about them, the possibility of their existence was standing. And on this assumption, why is it not permissible that the agent of these miracles is these intellects and souls? The difference between this question and the question of angels is that angels according to the theologians (al-mutakallimun) are something different from these intellects and souls. So we presented the question of angels according to what they believe regarding the existence of angels, and we presented this question here according to the doctrines of the philosophers regarding intellects and souls. The eighth possibility: That we say: There is no doubt that the bodies of this elemental world share in hyle (hayula). And that hyle is receptive to all forms and accidents... And if this is established, we say: The specification of each of these bodies with its particular quality and its particular form is either because that body was more worthy of receiving that quality and form than other bodies, or it was not so. The second is false. Otherwise it would necessitate that the specification of that body with that quality, while being equal to other bodies in receptivity and in lacking priority, would be a preponderance of one of the two sides of the possible over the other without a preponderator (murajjih), which is impossible. And since this division has been invalidated, it is established that the first division is true. So we say: And the specification of that body with that particular preparedness (isti'dad) must be due to another preparedness; ad infinitum. So if those preparednesses occur at once, it would necessitate the occurrence of causes and effects without end at once, which is impossible. And if they occur in succession, such that each previous preparedness is the cause of the occurrence of the subsequent preparedness, then the occurrence of this particular miracle which is a breach of custom would be among the necessary concomitants of the past states, which have no beginning. And then it would cease to be indicative of truthfulness. The summary: That if that body is equal to other bodies, and that time is equal to other times, in accepting that particular event, then the possible would have been preponderated without a preponderator. And if this is permissible, then why is it not permissible for a miracle to occur without any purpose at all? And that invalidates the claim that the miracle indicates truthfulness. Also: Either the occurrence of that event depends on that body being described with that particular preparedness, then the occurrence of this miracle would be among the necessary concomitants of the past states. And on this assumption, it ceases to be a proof of the truthfulness of the claimant.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents two possibilities (al-ih'timal al-sabi' and al-ih'timal al-thamin) that challenge the standard theological argument that miracles prove prophethood. The first possibility invokes the philosophers' doctrine of separate intellects and souls as possible agents of miracles, arguing that if these exist, they could be the true causes rather than divine intervention through a prophet. Al-Razi distinguishes this from the question of angels, which theologians accept as different entities. The second possibility is more detailed: it begins from the fact that all sublunar bodies share a common hyle (matter), which is receptive to all forms and accidents. The specification of each body with its particular form and quality is not due to any priority of that body, otherwise infinite regress would follow. Al-Razi argues that if the specification is not due to priority, then the body is equal to others, and thus the miracle would be a preponderance without preponderator, which is absurd. Alternatively, if the occurrence depends on a special preparedness in the body, then that preparedness requires another preparedness ad infinitum. If all these preparednesses happen at once, infinite causes and effects occur at once, impossible. If they occur in succession, the miracle becomes a necessary consequence of an infinite series of past states, hence no longer a miracle that indicates truthfulness. The conclusion is that if miracles could be explained by natural or celestial predispositions, they lose their evidentiary value.

Key Terms
عقول ونفوس (intellects and souls)
ملائكة (angels)
متكلمين (theologians)
فلاسفة (philosophers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Razi is asserting that intellects and souls definitely cause miracles.
Correction: He is only raising a possibility (ihtimal) that must be refuted before miracles can be used as proof.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh possibility, why might miracles not prove prophethood?
A) Because philosophers deny miracles altogether.
B) Because angels might cause them instead.
C) Because separate intellects and souls could be the agents.
D) Because the miracle might be a coincidence.

Key Takeaway
The seventh possibility shows that without refuting the existence of separate intellects and souls, miracles cannot be conclusive evidence for prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness signs of God's guidance in your life, do you acknowledge them as from Him alone, or do you subconsciously explain them away through natural causes? How does Al-Razi's challenge to easy proof confront your own tendency to avoid full accountability to the Creator?
?
If even miracles can be doubted without examining foundational assumptions, what does that say about the depth of your own faith? Are you willing to honestly entertain the possibilities Al-Razi raises, or do you find them threatening to your comfort?
?
Al-Razi here does not fear intellectual objections but uses them to strengthen the search for truth. What would it cost you to truly engage with doubts in your own belief—and what might you gain if you resolved them as he intended?

The Eighth Possibility: Infinite Regress of Preparedness
Al-Razi presents the eighth possibility: infinite regress of preparedness in bodies nullifies miracle's evidentiary value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that if a miracle depends on a special preparedness in the body, an infinite regress follows, making the miracle a necessary consequence of past states and thus not a proof of truthfulness.

Core Idea
If bodies need infinite preparedness, miracles become necessary, not evidentiary.

Al-Razi's eighth possibility delves into the nature of material bodies. All sublunar bodies share a common matter (hyle) that is receptive to forms. How does a particular body acquire a specific form? If it requires a special preparedness, that preparedness itself needs another, leading to an infinite regress. This lesson traces the argument and its conclusion that miracles lose their indicative power.

Guided Path
1
Read the eighth possibility passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. This is a longer argument with multiple steps: from shared hyle to specification, to priority or no priority, to infinite regress.
Note the key terms: هيولى (hyle), استعداد (preparedness), مرجح (preponderator).
2
Understand the initial division
Al-Razi starts: a body's particular form is either because it was more worthy (priority) or not. The latter leads to preponderance without preponderator, which is impossible. So priority must be true.
This is a classical kalam argument about sufficient reason.
3
Trace the infinite regress
If priority is true, the body's preparedness itself requires a prior preparedness, ad infinitum. This regress is analyzed in two ways: simultaneous (impossible) or successive (makes miracle a necessary consequent of past states). Either way, the miracle loses its evidentiary value.
4
Consider the conclusion
The final summary: if body and time are equal in receptivity, a miracle occurrence would be a preponderance without preponderator, absurd. Or if it depends on preparedness, it becomes part of an infinite chain, no longer a special sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في هذا السؤال . فقد جعلنا الأفلاك والكواكب ، أحياء ناطقة .. مختارة في الفعل والترك
والاحتمال السابع : اتفقت الفلاسفة على إثبات العقول والنفوس . فقبل إقامة الدلالة على إبطال القول بها ، كان احتمال وجودها قائماً . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فلم لا يجوز أن يكون فاعل هذه المعجزات هو هذه العقول والنفوس ؟ والفرق بين هذا السؤال وبين سؤال الملائكة : هو أن الملائكة عند المتكلمين شيء مغاير لهذه العقول والنفوس ، فأوردنا سؤال الملائكة على حسب ما يعتقدون في وجود الملائكة ، وأوردنا هذا السؤال ههنا على حسب مذاهب الفلاسفة في العقول والنفوس
·
الاحتمال الثامن : أن نقول : لا شك أن أجسام هذا العالم العنصري ، مشتركة في الهيولى. وتلك الهيولى قابلة لجميع الصور والأعراض على البدن وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : اختصاص كل واحد من هذه الأجسام بصفته المعينة وصورته المعينة ، إما أن يكون لأجل أن ذلك الجسم كان أولى بقبول تلك الصفة والصورة من سائر الأجسام أو لم يكن كذلك . والثاني باطل . وإلا لزم أن يكون اختصاص ذلك الجسم بتلك الصفة مع كونه مساوياً لسائر الأجسام في القبول ، وفي عدم الأولوية ، يكون رجحانا ، لأحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر ، لا لمرجح ، وهو محال . ولما بطل هذا القسم ، ثبت أن القسم الأول حق . فنقول : واختصاص ذلك الجسم بذلك الاستعداد الخاص ، لا بد وأن يكون لأجل استعداد آخر ؛ إلى غير النهاية ، فتلك الاستعدادات إن حصلت دفعة واحدة ، لزم حصول أسباب ومسببات لا نهاية لها ، دفعة واحدة . وهو محال ، وإن حصلت على سبيل التعاقب ، وهو أن يكون كل استعداد سابق ، علة الحصول الاستعداد اللاحق ، فحينئذ يكون حصول هذا المعجز المعين الذي هو فعل خارق للعادة من لوازم الأحوال السالفة ، التي لا أول لها . وحينئذ تخرج عن كونها دالة على الصدق
·
والحاصل : أنه إن كان ذلك الجسم مساوياً ، لسائر الأجسام ، وكان ذلك الوقت مساوياً لسائر الأوقات، في قبول ذلك الحادث المعين ، فحينئذ قد ترجح الممكن لا المرجح . وإذا جاز هذا ، فلم لا يجوز حدوث المعجز ، لا لغرض أصلاً ؟ وذلك يبطل القول بدلالة المعجز على الصدق .
وأيضاً : إما أن يتوقف حدوث ذلك الحادث على كون ذلك الجسم موصوفاً بذلك الاستعداد الخاص ، فحينئذ يكون حدوث هذا المعجز من لوازم الأحوال السالفة . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فإنه يخرج عن كونه دليلا على صدق المدعي
As for this question, we have made the celestial spheres and planets, living rational beings... free will in action and omission. The seventh possibility: The philosophers agreed on affirming intellects and souls. So before establishing the proof for invalidating the claim about them, the possibility of their existence was standing. And on this assumption, why is it not permissible that the agent of these miracles is these intellects and souls? The difference between this question and the question of angels is that angels according to the theologians (al-mutakallimun) are something different from these intellects and souls. So we presented the question of angels according to what they believe regarding the existence of angels, and we presented this question here according to the doctrines of the philosophers regarding intellects and souls. The eighth possibility: That we say: There is no doubt that the bodies of this elemental world share in hyle (hayula). And that hyle is receptive to all forms and accidents... And if this is established, we say: The specification of each of these bodies with its particular quality and its particular form is either because that body was more worthy of receiving that quality and form than other bodies, or it was not so. The second is false. Otherwise it would necessitate that the specification of that body with that quality, while being equal to other bodies in receptivity and in lacking priority, would be a preponderance of one of the two sides of the possible over the other without a preponderator (murajjih), which is impossible. And since this division has been invalidated, it is established that the first division is true. So we say: And the specification of that body with that particular preparedness (isti'dad) must be due to another preparedness; ad infinitum. So if those preparednesses occur at once, it would necessitate the occurrence of causes and effects without end at once, which is impossible. And if they occur in succession, such that each previous preparedness is the cause of the occurrence of the subsequent preparedness, then the occurrence of this particular miracle which is a breach of custom would be among the necessary concomitants of the past states, which have no beginning. And then it would cease to be indicative of truthfulness. The summary: That if that body is equal to other bodies, and that time is equal to other times, in accepting that particular event, then the possible would have been preponderated without a preponderator. And if this is permissible, then why is it not permissible for a miracle to occur without any purpose at all? And that invalidates the claim that the miracle indicates truthfulness. Also: Either the occurrence of that event depends on that body being described with that particular preparedness, then the occurrence of this miracle would be among the necessary concomitants of the past states. And on this assumption, it ceases to be a proof of the truthfulness of the claimant.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents two possibilities (al-ih'timal al-sabi' and al-ih'timal al-thamin) that challenge the standard theological argument that miracles prove prophethood. The first possibility invokes the philosophers' doctrine of separate intellects and souls as possible agents of miracles, arguing that if these exist, they could be the true causes rather than divine intervention through a prophet. Al-Razi distinguishes this from the question of angels, which theologians accept as different entities. The second possibility is more detailed: it begins from the fact that all sublunar bodies share a common hyle (matter), which is receptive to all forms and accidents. The specification of each body with its particular form and quality is not due to any priority of that body, otherwise infinite regress would follow. Al-Razi argues that if the specification is not due to priority, then the body is equal to others, and thus the miracle would be a preponderance without preponderator, which is absurd. Alternatively, if the occurrence depends on a special preparedness in the body, then that preparedness requires another preparedness ad infinitum. If all these preparednesses happen at once, infinite causes and effects occur at once, impossible. If they occur in succession, the miracle becomes a necessary consequence of an infinite series of past states, hence no longer a miracle that indicates truthfulness. The conclusion is that if miracles could be explained by natural or celestial predispositions, they lose their evidentiary value.

Key Terms
هيولى (hyle)
استعداد (preparedness)
مرجح (preponderator)
معجز (miracle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Razi is endorsing natural determinism and denying miracles altogether.
Correction: He is showing that if the miraculous event is explained by natural preparedness, it loses its role as a special proof; he is not denying that miracles occur but questioning their evidentiary value.

Checkpoint
According to the eighth possibility, if a body's special preparedness for a miracle requires an infinite regress of prior preparednesses, what happens to the miracle's evidentiary value?
A) It becomes a stronger proof.
B) It becomes impossible.
C) It becomes a necessary consequence of past states, no longer indicative.
D) It becomes a random event.

Key Takeaway
The eighth possibility uses the concept of hyle and infinite regress to show that if a miracle depends on a natural preparedness chain, it cannot serve as a unique proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Razi argues that if a miracle is a necessary consequence of an infinite chain, it ceases to be a proof. Does your faith rely on miracles as evidence? If that evidence were stripped away, what would remain? Are you prepared to have your certainty rooted in Allah alone, not in signs?
?
When you hear of a miraculous event, do you instinctively seek a natural explanation or accept it as divine intervention? What does your response reveal about the state of your heart? Will you train yourself to see the Hand of Allah in all things, even the ordinary?
?
The eighth possibility forces you to examine the basis of your trust in the Prophet's ﷺ truthfulness. Is it the miracles themselves, or the One who sent them? If your whole faith depended on a single miracle that could be explained away, would it crumble? Commit today to building your faith on the unshakeable foundation of tawheed and submission, not on spectacular events.

Al-Razi's Systematic Classification of Miracle Agents
Al-Razi provides a systematic classification of miracle agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi systematically classifies all possible agents of miracles into a dichotomous tree, covering natural, celestial, angelic, spiritual, and demonic explanations.

Core Idea
Al-Razi maps every possible non-divine source of miracles into a clear taxonomy.

Al-Razi, in his characteristic analytical style, does not merely list alternatives but organizes them into a logical tree. This classification is crucial for understanding the philosophical challenge to prophethood: if miracles can be explained through natural or celestial causes, their evidential value is undermined. This passage lays out the full range of alternatives that a defender of prophethood must address.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let al-Razi's taxonomic structure emerge naturally.
Notice the binary divisions: prophet vs. other, corporeal vs. incorporeal, etc.
2
Identify the first division
The top-level division is between the prophet himself and some other agent. Al-Razi then subdivides each branch. Start by noting this primary split.
3
Trace the corporeal branch
Follow the 'other' branch into corporeal substances (elemental, celestial, mixed, and angelic bodies). List each subcategory and its example.
Angels are described as luminous celestial bodies capable of heavy tasks.
4
Trace the incorporeal branch
Follow the 'other' branch into incorporeal substances (lower spirits/devils and upper spirits/intellects and souls). Note how al-Razi covers all possibilities.
This branch shows that philosophical explanations include both demonic and angelic spiritual agencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطريق ضبط هذه الاحتمالات أن نقول : فاعل هذه المعجزات ، إما أن يكون هو النبي أو غيره . فإن كان هو النبي ، فيحتمل أن يكون اقتداره على خلقها لأجل مزاجه المخصوص، وأن يكون لنفسه المخصوصة . وأما إن كان غيره فذلك الغير ، إما أن يكون جوهراً جسمانياً أو جوهراً مجرداً. فإن كان جسماً فهو إما أن يكون جسماً ، عنصرياً وهو الدواء المخصوص ، أو جسماً فلكياً وهو القرانات ، والاتصالات الحاصلة بحسب السيارات والثوابت ، أو ممزوجاً من القسمين ، أو جسماً مغايراً لهذين القسمين ، وهو الذي يقال : إن الملائكة أجسام نورانية علوية قادرة على الأعمال الشاقة . وأما إن كان ذلك الغير روحانياً ، فإما أن تكون هي الأرواح السفلية ، الشياطين . أو الأرواح العلوية ، وهي : العقول والنفوس . والله أعلم .
The way to systematize these possibilities is to say: The agent of these miracles is either the prophet or other than him. If it is the prophet, then it is possible that his power to create them is due to his particular temperament (mizaj), or due to his particular soul. And if it is other than him, then that other is either a corporeal substance (jawhar jismani) or an incorporeal substance (jawhar mujarrad). If it is a body, then it is either an elemental body, which is the particular medicine, or a celestial body, which are the conjunctions (qiranat) and aspects (ittisalat) occurring according to the planets and fixed stars, or a mixture of the two types, or a body different from these two types, which is what is said: that angels are luminous celestial bodies capable of heavy tasks. And if that other is spiritual (ruhani), then it is either the lower spirits, i.e., devils, or the upper spirits, which are the intellects and souls. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a systematic classification (taqsīm) of all possible agents of miracles. Al-Razi organizes the possibilities into a dichotomous tree. The first division is whether the agent is the prophet himself or something else. If the prophet, his power may be due to his specific bodily temperament (mizāj) or his specific soul (nafs). If the agent is not the prophet, it is either a corporeal substance (jawhar jismānī) or an incorporeal substance (jawhar mujarrad). Corporeal agents are further divided into elemental bodies (e.g., a specific medicine), celestial bodies (e.g., planetary conjunctions and aspects), a mixture of both, or another kind of body (angels, described as luminous celestial bodies capable of heavy tasks). Incorporeal agents are divided into lower spirits (devils) and upper spirits (intellects and souls). This classification shows the breadth of alternatives that philosophers and others have proposed to explain miracles without divine intervention, thereby challenging the standard proof of prophethood. Al-Razi ends with 'And God knows best,' indicating humility before the full scope of possibilities.

Key Terms
جوهر جسماني
جوهر مجرد
قرانات
اتصالات
أرواح
مزاج
نفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Razi is endorsing these alternatives as valid explanations of miracles.
Correction: Al-Razi is merely cataloging the range of possible objections that have been raised against the miraculous proof of prophethood. He is not affirming any of them as true.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's taxonomy reveals that the miracle proof must contend with multiple natural and metaphysical alternative explanations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Al-Razi ends his systematic classification with 'And God knows best.' How often do you approach matters of faith—especially difficult ones like miracles—with genuine humility, acknowledging that your own reasoning is limited? Is there an area of your belief where you have been too confident in your own understanding, forgetting that God's knowledge encompasses all possibilities? The Miracle as Contingent and Its Indication of Truthfulness
The author defines the miracle and gives two arguments that it ceases to be proof if necessary from past states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why some philosophers argue that miracles cannot be definitive proofs of truthfulness, and how the author presents two arguments to that effect.

Core Idea
Miracles lose their evidential power if they are necessary consequences of past states.

This passage challenges the common assumption that miracles are always clear proofs of divine intervention. The author argues that if a miracle is a necessary outcome of a body's past states, then it cannot serve as a sign of truthfulness. Read on to see two distinct arguments that support this claim.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of miracle
Start by reading the passage's definition of a miracle as an extraordinary act that is a necessary consequence of past states.
2
Grasp the first argument: preference without preponderator
Consider the hypothetical: if the body and time are equivalent to others, then the miracle's occurrence would be a preference without a preponderator, which invalidates its purpose.
This argument shows that without a specific need, the miracle could be arbitrary.
3
Analyze the second argument: the dichotomy
Examine the either-or scenario: either the miracle depends on a specific preparedness (making it necessary) or it does not (making it arbitrary). Either way, it fails as a proof.
This reinforces the conclusion that miracles are not reliable signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجز المعين الذي هو فعل خارق للعادة من لوازم الأحوال السالفة ، التي لا أول لها . وحينئذ تخرج عن كونها دالة على الصدق .
والحاصل : أنه إن كان ذلك الجسم مساوياً لسائر الأجسام ، وكان ذلك الوقت مساوياً لسائر الأوقات، في قبول ذلك الحادث المعين ، فحينئذ قد ترجح الممكن لا المرجح . وإذا جاز هذا ، فلم لا يجوز حدوث المعجز لا لغرض أصلاً ؟ وذلك يبطل القول بدلالة المعجز على الصدق .
وأيضاً : إما أن يتوقف حدوث ذلك الحادث على كون ذلك الجسم موصوفاً بذلك الاستعداد الخاص ، فحينئذ يكون حدوث هذا المعجز من لوازم الأحوال السالفة . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فإنه يخرج عن كونه دليلاً على صدق المدعي
The specific miracle which is an extraordinary act is from the necessary consequences of past states, which have no beginning. Then it ceases to be indicative of truthfulness.
The conclusion: that if that body is equal to other bodies, and that time is equal to other times, in accepting that specific event, then the possible has been preferred without a preponderator. And if this is permissible, then why is it not permissible for a miracle to occur without any purpose at all? And that invalidates the statement that the miracle indicates truthfulness.
Also: either the occurrence of that event depends on that body being described with that specific preparedness, then the occurrence of this miracle is from the necessary consequences of past states. And on this supposition, it ceases to be a proof of the truthfulness of the claimant.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents a definition and two arguments regarding the evidential value of miracles. It begins by defining the specific miracle (al-mu'jiz al-mu'ayyan) as an extraordinary act that is a necessary consequence (lazim) of past states that have no beginning. On this definition, the miracle would not be a proof of truthfulness because it is necessary, not free. The author then states the conclusion (al-hasil) in the form of a hypothetical: if the body receiving the miracle is equal to all other bodies, and the time is equal to all other times in accepting that event, then the possible (al-mumkin) has been preferred without a preponderator (murajjih). If this is possible, then a miracle could occur without any purpose, which would invalidate its indication of truth. The second argument ('aydan) presents a dichotomy: either the miracle's occurrence depends on a specific preparedness of the body, in which case it is a necessary consequence of past states and thus not a proof of the claimant's truthfulness, or it does not, in which case the first argument applies. The passage thus undermines the certainty of miracles as proofs by showing that under certain assumptions they could be arbitrary or necessary.

Key Terms
معجز
خارق للعادة
لازم
دال على الصدق
ترجيح بلا مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are always definitive proofs of a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The passage shows that if a miracle is a necessary consequence of past states or occurs without a preponderator, it ceases to be a proof of truthfulness.

Checkpoint
If the miracle is a necessary consequence of past states, what happens to its indication of truth?
A) It becomes a proof of truth.
B) It ceases to be a proof of truth.
C) It becomes impossible.
D) It becomes a matter of habit.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are not automatically proofs of truthfulness; their evidential value depends on whether they are necessary or free acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage argues that if a miracle could occur without purpose, it loses its evidential value. In your own life, have you ever accepted something as a sign from God without critically examining whether it truly points to Him? How can you train yourself to discern genuine signs from coincidences?
?
If the evidential value of miracles can be philosophically challenged, what then is the ultimate basis for your faith? Does your belief rest on such arguments or on a direct, unshakeable connection with the Divine? What steps will you take to deepen that connection so that no argument can shake it?

Agents of Miracles: A Systematic Enumeration
The author classifies possible doers of miracles into prophets and others, with subcategories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational classification of possible agents of miracles according to Islamic theological reasoning, distinguishing between prophetic and non-prophetic sources and their subcategories.

Core Idea
Miracles do not accidentally prove prophethood — their agent must be identified first.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah provides a systematic method for enumerating all possible agents of miracles. Before evaluating a claim of prophethood, one must consider whether the extraordinary act is performed by the prophet himself or by another entity, and then further categorize the nature of that entity. This classification is essential for analyzing the validity of prophethood claims by eliminating alternative explanations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own branching structure come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage uses a logical tree-like structure.
2
Identify the two main branches
The passage starts by dividing the agent of miracles into two possibilities: the prophet himself or someone else. Mark these as the primary categories.
3
Explore the sub-branches under 'someone else'
Under the non-prophetic category, the author distinguishes bodily and non-bodily substances. Then each of these has further subdivisions. Trace these carefully.
Pay attention to the four types of bodies and two types of spirits.
4
Reflect on the theological purpose
Consider why this classification is important for proving prophethood. It shows that miracles could have alternative explanations, so prophets must be distinguished by additional criteria.
This connects to the broader discussion of miracles as proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطريق ضبط هذه الاحتمالات أن نقول : فاعل هذه المعجزات ، إما أن يكون هو النبي أو غيره . فإن كان هو النبي ، فيحتمل أن يكون اقتداره على خلقها لأجل مزاجه المخصوص، وأن يكون لنفسه المخصوصة . وأما إن كان غيره فذلك الغير ، إما أن يكون جوهراً جسمانياً أو جوهراً مجرداً. فإن كان جسماً فهو إما أن يكون جسماً عنصرياً وهو الدواء المخصوص ، أو جسماً فلكياً وهو القرانات والاتصالات الحاصلة بحسب السيارات والثوابت ، أو ممزوجاً من القسمين ، أو جسماً مغايراً لهذين القسمين ، وهو الذي يقال : إن الملائكة أجسام نورانية علوية قادرة على الأعمال الشاقة . وأما إن كان ذلك الغير روحانياً ، فإما أن يكون هي الأرواح السفلية الشياطين . أو الأرواح العلوية وهي : العقول والنفوس . والله أعلم .
The way to regulate these possibilities is that we say: the doer of these miracles is either the prophet or someone else. If it is the prophet, then it is possible that his power to create them is due to his specific temperament, or due to his specific soul. But if it is someone else, then that other is either a bodily substance or a non-bodily substance. If it is a body, then it is either an elemental body which is the specific medicine, or a celestial body which is the conjunctions and aspects occurring according to the planets and fixed stars, or a mixture of the two kinds, or a body different from these two kinds, which is that which is said: the angels are luminous celestial bodies capable of heavy tasks. And if that other is spiritual, then it is either the lower spirits, the devils, or the higher spirits, which are: the intellects and souls. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides a systematic method (tariq dabt) for enumerating the possibilities regarding the agent of miracles. It begins by stating that the doer (fa'il) of miracles is either the prophet himself or someone else (ghayruhu). If it is the prophet, his ability could be due to his specific temperament (mizaj) or his specific soul (nafs). If it is someone else, that other is either a bodily substance (jawhar jismani) or a non-bodily substance (jawhar mujarrad). If it is a body, it falls into four categories: elemental (like a specific medicine), celestial (like planetary conjunctions), a mixture of both, or a different kind (like angels, described as luminous celestial bodies capable of heavy tasks). If it is spiritual (ruhani), it is either lower spirits (the devils) or higher spirits (the intellects and souls). The author concludes with 'Allah knows best.' This classification helps in analyzing claims of prophethood by considering all possible sources of extraordinary acts.

Key Terms
فاعل
معجزات
مزاج
نفس
جوهر جسماني
جوهر مجرد
جسم عنصري
جسم فلكي
ملائكة
أرواح سفلية
أرواح علوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All miracles are directly caused by God without any intermediary agent.
Correction: Islamic theologians consider that miracles may be caused by prophets themselves (through temperament or soul) or even by other beings such as angels, jinn, or celestial bodies, though ultimately all power comes from God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the agent of a miracle is a non-bodily spirit, what are the two subcategories?
A) Angels and demons
B) Lower spirits (devils) and higher spirits (intellects and souls)
C) Celestial bodies and elemental bodies
D) Prophetic souls and demonic souls

Key Takeaway
The classification of miracle agents is a rational tool to evaluate prophethood claims by systematically eliminating alternative explanations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an event that seems miraculous, do you instinctively attribute it to God or a prophet without considering other natural or spiritual agents? How would this classification challenge you to be more intellectually honest in your analysis?
?
Have you ever witnessed something you considered a 'miracle' from someone who claimed prophethood or sainthood? Did you ever stop to question whether their temperament, soul, or even a celestial alignment could have produced it? How would this passage change your approach to verifying such claims?
?
If the possibility exists that a miracle could be performed by a devil or a lower spirit, how does that affect your trust in spiritual experiences? Are you willing to re-examine your past spiritual encounters through the lens of this classification, even if it means admitting you might have been deceived?
