Refutation of Jewish Tawatur Claim on Mosaic Law
Mutakallimun refute Jewish claim of tawatur for Mosaic law's abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mutakallimun refuted the Jewish claim of tawatur for the unabolished Mosaic law by pointing to the historical interruption caused by Nebuchadnezzar's massacre.

Core Idea
Tawatur requires both large numbers and uninterrupted transmission.

The mutakallimun encountered a Jewish argument claiming that Moses had declared his law eternal, and this was transmitted via tawatur. To refute this, they invoked a historical catastrophe: Nebuchadnezzar's destruction of the Jewish community. This lesson unpacks that refutation and highlights the conditions necessary for a genuine tawatur report.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic and English versions. Notice how the mutakallimun's answer is structured: they first state the Jewish claim, then present the historical fact, and finally conclude that the report fails the tawatur test.
2
Identify the two key elements
The Jewish claim: Moses said 'My law shall never be abrogated' and it was supposedly transmitted by tawatur. The mutakallimun's counter: Nebuchadnezzar killed most of the Israelites, leaving only a small group that could conspire to lie.
3
Understand the condition of tawatur
Tawatur requires a large number of narrators in every generation such that collusion on falsehood is impossible. After the massacre, the surviving community was too small to meet this condition, breaking the chain.
Thus the Jewish report loses its status as mutawatir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المتكلمين أجابوا عن ادعاء اليهود حصول التواتر في أن موسى عليه السلام قال: « إن شريعتي لا تصير منسوخة »، بأن قالوا: إن بخت نصر قتلهم بالكلية، ولم يبق منهم إلا عدد قليل يمكن إطباقهم على الكذب. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فقد خرجت روايتهم عن حد التواتر.
And know that the mutakallimun answered the claim of the Jews of the occurrence of tawatur that Moses, peace be upon him, said: 'My law shall not become abrogated,' by saying: Nebuchadnezzar killed them entirely, and only a small number remained who could be colluded to lie. And if that is the case, then their report has left the limit of tawatur.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents the response of the mutakallimun (scholars of kalam) to a specific Jewish claim. The Jews claimed to have tawatur that Moses declared his law would never be abrogated. The mutakallimun refute this by arguing that the chain of transmission was broken by Nebuchadnezzar's massacre of the Israelites, leaving only a small number of survivors. A small group can potentially conspire to lie, so the condition of tawatur (which requires a large number impossible to collude on falsehood) is not met. Therefore, the supposed tawatur is invalid, and the Jewish claim fails. The passage demonstrates how mutakallimun critically examine claims of tawatur by considering historical interruptions in the transmission chain.

Key Terms

The mutakallimun demonstrated that an interruption in the chain of transmission, such as a devastating event, can invalidate a claim of tawatur.

Refuting the Jewish Claim of Tawatur on Moses' Law
The mutakallimun refute the Jewish claim of tawatur on Moses' law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two key arguments used by Muslim theologians to refute the Jewish claim that Moses' law cannot be abrogated.

Core Idea
The Jewish claim of tawatur is refuted by both historical disruption and scriptural prophecy.

The Jews claimed that they have tawatur from Moses that his law will never be abrogated. Muslim theologians responded with two powerful arguments: one historical, showing the chain of transmission was broken, and one scriptural, pointing to Moses' own prophecy of a future prophet. This lesson examines both refutations and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the two distinct arguments presented.
The passage includes both the historical and scriptural arguments.
2
Understand the historical argument
Identify how Nebuchadnezzar's massacre broke the chain of transmission, making tawatur impossible.
The key phrase is 'بخت نصر قتلهم بالكلية'.
3
Analyze the scriptural argument
Examine how the Torah's prophecy of a prophet like Moses implies abrogation. Note the different interpretations by Christians and Muslims.
The prophecy is from Deuteronomy 18:15.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these arguments are effective against the Jewish claim and how they defend the Islamic belief in final prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المتكلمين . أجابوا عن ادعاء اليهود : حصول التواتر في أن موسى عليه السلام قال : « إن شريعتي لا تصير منسوخة ، بأن قالوا : إن بخت نصر » قتلهم بالكلية ، ولم يبق منهم إلا عدد قليل ، يمكن إطباقهم على الكذب . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فقد خرجت روايتهم عن حد التواتر (4) . الإجابة الصحيحة على أن موسى لم يقل : شريعتي لا تصير منسوخة : أن في التوراة نبوءات أخبر بها موسى عن مجيء نبي من بعده ناسخ الشريعته . ومنها في الأصحاح الثامن عشر من سفر التثنية : و يقيم لك الحرب إلهك نبياً من وسطك من إخوتك مثلى له تسعون . الخ فقوله : ه له تسمعون ، يدل على أن بني إسرائيل مكلفون بسماع كلام النبي المنتظر ، حتى ولو أمرهم بترك شريعة موسى. ويدعي النصارى : أن المشار إليه بهذه النبوءة هو عيسى عليه السلام والنص لا يشير إليه لأنه من بني إسرائيل وقوله : ( من إخوتك ، تعني جنساً غير بني إسرائيل ويقول المسلمون : إنه محمد لأن التوراة نصت على بركة لآل إسماعيل [ تكوين ١٧ : ٢٠ ] والبركة تعني : الملك والنبوة وإسماعيل أخ الإسحاق عليهما السلام

And since that is the case, their narration has exited the limit of tawatur. The correct answer to that Moses did not say: My law shall not be abrogated, is that in the Torah there are prophecies that Moses informed about the coming of a prophet after him who would abrogate his law. Among them in chapter 18 of Deuteronomy: 'The Lord your God will raise up for you a prophet from among you, from your brethren, like me; to him you shall listen,' etc. So his saying 'to him you shall listen' indicates that the Children of Israel are obligated to listen to the words of the awaited prophet, even if he commands them to leave the law of Moses. And the Christians claim that the one referred to in this prophecy is Jesus, peace be upon him, but the text does not refer to him because he is from the Children of Israel, and his saying 'from your brethren' means a race other than the Children of Israel, and the Muslims say that it is Muhammad because the Torah stipulated a blessing for the descendants of Ishmael [Genesis 17:20] and blessing means kingship and prophethood, and Ishmael is the brother of Isaac, peace be upon them.

Commentary
This passage records the mutakallimun's response to the Jewish claim that they have tawatur from Moses that his law will never be abrogated. The mutakallimun argue that the Jewish transmission chain was broken when Nebuchadnezzar massacred the Israelites, leaving only a small number who could conspire to lie, so their narration no longer meets the conditions of tawatur. The subsequent note (4) provides an alternative refutation: Moses himself prophesied a future prophet like him, implying abrogation. The note discusses the interpretation of Deuteronomy 18:15, with Christians claiming it refers to Jesus and Muslims claiming it refers to Muhammad.

Allah Cast Jesus' Likeness on Another Man
Mutakallimun explain substitution to refute crucifixion claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic response to the claim of Jesus' crucifixion: that Allah substituted another man who resembled Jesus, preventing the actual crucifixion.

Core Idea
Allah protected Jesus by casting his likeness on another, causing confusion.

The claim that Jesus was crucified is one of the most significant points of contention between Islam and Christianity. The mutakallimun present a clear response: Allah did not allow Jesus to be killed but instead made another man appear exactly like him. This lesson explores that answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the mutakallimun frame their response as an answer to a claim.
The passage is very concise—every word matters.
2
Identify the two key terms
Find the terms 'الشبهة' (confusion/doubt) and 'إلقاء الصورة' (casting of likeness). Understand how they relate: the casting of likeness causes the confusion.
Shubha (confusion) is a key concept in Islamic theology for resolving apparent contradictions.
3
Understand the argument structure
The passage presents: Claim (Jews and Christians say Jesus was killed/crucified) -> Response (Allah cast likeness on another man) -> Result (this caused confusion). Identify each part.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this substitution is important: it affirms Allah's power to protect His prophets and clarifies that Jesus was not actually killed.
This aligns with the Quranic verse: 'And they did not kill him, nor did they crucify him; but it was made to appear so to them.' (4:157)

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجابوا عن نقل اليهود والنصاري عن قتل عيسى عليه السلام وصلبه : بأن الله تعالى ألقى صورة عيسى عليه السلام على إنسان آخر فلهذا السبب حصلت هذه الشبهة
And they answered the transmission of the Jews and Christians about the killing and crucifixion of Jesus, peace be upon him: that Allah the Exalted cast the likeness of Jesus, peace be upon him, onto another man, and for this reason this confusion occurred.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the mutakallimun's response to the Jewish and Christian claim that Jesus was killed and crucified. They explain that Allah cast the likeness of Jesus onto another man (substitution), which caused confusion, so the actual event did not happen to Jesus but to someone who resembled him. This is the standard Islamic doctrine regarding the crucifixion.

Key Terms

إلقاء الصورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Jesus was actually crucified and died on the cross.
Correction: According to the mutakallimun, Allah cast the likeness of Jesus onto another man, so the crucifixion occurred to that substitute, not to Jesus himself.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Islamic response to the crucifixion claim is based on divine substitution: Allah made another man resemble Jesus, causing the confusion.

Why Miracles Cannot Support Dualists
The mutakallimun deny miracles for Zardusht and Mani due to their disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the mutakallimun argued that miracles cannot appear at the hands of those who reject tawhid (monotheism).

Core Idea
A miracle can only authenticate a true prophet, not a dualist.

The Magians and Manicheans claimed that Zardusht and Mani performed miracles. The mutakallimun refuted this by pointing out that prophethood requires true knowledge of God. Since Zardusht and Mani believed in two eternal principles, they were guilty of disbelief, and miracles cannot support a false claim. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style used to deliver a logical argument.
2
Understand the key premise
The argument links prophethood to monotheism. Identify the connection: prophethood is derived from knowledge of God, and dualism contradicts that knowledge.
This premise is central to the refutation.
3
Apply the principle
Consider why this argument would prevent miracles from being used to support any false religion. How does it protect the integrity of prophethood?
Think about the broader implications for claims of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجابوا عن ادعاء المجوس والمانوية ظهور المعجزات على « زردشت ، و ه ماني » ] بأن قالوا : النبوة متفرعة على معرفة الإله ، وه زردشت ، و ه ماني (١) : ] أثبتا للعالم المين. وهذا من أعظم أنواع الكفر . والكافر يمتنع ظهور المعجزات على يده
And they answered the claim of the Magians and Manicheans about the appearance of miracles upon Zardusht and Mani, by saying: Prophethood is derived from knowledge of God, and Zardusht and Mani affirmed two eternal principles for the world. This is among the greatest types of disbelief. And a disbeliever cannot have miracles appear at his hand.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage records the mutakallimun's response to the Magians and Manicheans who claim miracles for Zardusht (Zoroaster) and Mani. The mutakallimun argue that prophethood depends on knowledge of God (true monotheism). Since Zardusht and Mani affirmed dualism (two eternal principles), they are guilty of the greatest disbelief, and therefore miracles cannot occur at the hands of a disbeliever. The argument is that authentic miracles can only support true prophets, and dualists are not true prophets.

Key Terms
النبوة
المعجزات
الكفر
المجوس

زردشت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that miracles can prove anyone's prophethood, regardless of their beliefs.
Correction: The mutakallimun argue that miracles only support true prophets, and a dualist cannot be a true prophet because they reject the foundation of prophethood: knowledge of the one God.

Checkpoint

A) Because their miracles are not recorded in reliable sources
B) Because they were not prophets but philosophers
C) Because they affirmed dualism, which is disbelief
D) Because their followers exaggerated their abilities

Key Takeaway
Miracles can only appear at the hands of a true prophet, and a true prophet must believe in one God; thus, dualists cannot perform miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage warns that a disbeliever cannot produce a true miracle. Reflect: Have you ever attributed spiritual authority to someone whose core beliefs contradict tawheed? What concrete step can you take this week to ensure you only seek guidance from those who uphold God's oneness in the most absolute sense?

Denying the Necessity of Fame for Great Events
The opponent denies the necessity of fame and offers Muhammad's miracles as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponent in the tawatur debate denies the necessity of fame for great events and offers Muhammad's miracles as a counterexample.

Core Idea
Great events can be transmitted by few; fame is not required.

The opponent now directly challenges the mutakallimun's assumption that great events must become widely known. Using the example of Muhammad's miracles, which were reported only by one or two companions, he shows that historical transmission does not always follow a pattern of widespread fame. This lesson examines the first part of his counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's response to the population decrease argument
Start by reading the opponent's reply to the mutakallimun's claim about the Jews' decrease. Notice how he turns the logic around: if decrease is possible for Jews, it is possible for all tawatur.
2
Identify the opponent's stance on the necessity of fame
The opponent distinguishes between 'may become famous' and 'must become famous'. Find this distinction and understand why he rejects the necessity.
This is the core of his response.
3
Examine the first proof from Muhammad's miracles
Read the list of miracles (water from fingers, feeding many, etc.). Note how these are presented as great events yet transmitted by few. This serves as a direct counterexample.
The miracles are well-known in Islamic tradition but were initially reported by few.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The opponent concludes that the claim 'great events must be transmitted' is weak. Consider the strength of this rebuttal within the larger debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجاب القائل عن هذه الأجوبة : فقال : أما قولكم : إنه قل عدد اليهود في زمان ( بخت نصر ، فنقول : لما جاز هذا ، فلم لا يجوز مثله في جميع أنواع التواتر ؟ فإن قالوا : لو وقع ذلك لاشتهر ، لأن الوقائع العظيمة يجب اشتهارها ، بدليل : أنه لما حصلت هذه الواقعة في دين اليهود ، اشتهرت فيما بين الخلق . قلنا : لا نزاع في أن هذه الوقائع العظيمة قد تشتهر . فأما دعوى أنه يجب اشتهارها فهذا غير واجب . والدليل عليه من وجوه : الأول : إن معجزات محمد عليه السلام . مثل : انفجار الماء من بين أصابعه ، وإشباع الخلق الكثير من الطعام القليل ، وانقلاع الشجرة من أصلها ، وانشقاق القمر ، وكلام الذئب : وقائع عظيمة [ متعالية جداً ، يحدث (۲) ] هناك مانع يمنع من نقلها ، مع أنه لم يرو هذه الوقائع إلا الواحد والاثنان . فثبت : أن قولكم : إن الوقائع العظيمة يجب نقلها : ضعيف . الثاني : إن شعائر الصلوات كانت ظاهرة بادية مدة ثلاثة وعشرين سنة ثم إنها ما نقلت كما ينبغي ، فإنهم اختلفوا في كون الإقامة مثناه أو فرادى ، واختلفوا في قراءة ( بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، واختلفوا في سائر الشرائط
Then the speaker answered these answers and said: As for your saying that the number of Jews decreased in the time of Nebuchadnezzar, we say: Since this is possible, why is its like not possible in all types of tawatur? If they say: If that had occurred it would have become famous, because great events must become famous, evidenced by the fact that when this event occurred in the religion of the Jews, it became famous among the people. We say: There is no dispute that these great events may become famous. As for the claim that they must become famous, this is not necessary. The proof for it is from several aspects: The first: Indeed the miracles of Muhammad, peace be upon him, such as the gushing of water from between his fingers, the feeding of a great multitude from a small amount of food, the uprooting of a tree from its root, the splitting of the moon, and the speech of the wolf, are great events [very sublime, there occurred] an impediment preventing their transmission, and yet these events were not transmitted except by one or two. So it is established that your saying that great events must be transmitted is weak. The second: Indeed the rites of the prayers were manifest and apparent for a period of twenty-three years, yet they were not transmitted as they should have been, for they differed over whether the iqama is said twice or singly, and they differed over the recitation of 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', and they differed over the rest of the conditions.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the opponent's counter-response to the mutakallimun's previous answers. The opponent first challenges the argument about the Jewish population decrease, arguing that if it is possible for the Jews to decrease, it is possible in all types of tawatur. Then the opponent refutes the claim that great events must become widely known, using two examples from Islamic tradition: first, Muhammad's miracles (water from fingers, feeding many, uprooting tree, splitting moon, wolf speaking) were only transmitted by one or two individuals despite being great events, disproving the necessity of widespread transmission. Second, the rites of prayer were practiced openly for 23 years yet were not transmitted uniformly, as shown by differences in iqama and basmala. The passage cuts off before the third point.

التواتر
الاشتهار
المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Great events must be transmitted by tawatur (widespread, continuous report).
Correction: The opponent shows that Muhammad's miracles were transmitted by only one or two, yet they are great events. Therefore, fame is not a necessary condition for the truth of a report.

Checkpoint

The Prayer Rites as a Counterexample
The opponent argues that even the widely practiced prayer rites were not transmitted without disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponent uses the prayer rites (practiced openly for 23 years) to argue that even apparent practices were not transmitted uniformly, undermining the mutakallimun's argument.

Core Idea
Even visibly performed rites can have contested transmission.

The opponent's second proof focuses on the rites of prayer, which were performed publicly for 23 years. Despite their visibility, Muslims disagreed on details like the iqama and basmala. This shows that even widespread, continuous practices can lack tawatur in their details, further weakening the mutakallimun's claim.

These are matters of ritual practice, not obscure historical events.
3
Understand the implication
If such a public and continuous practice as prayer was not transmitted with full agreement, then the claim that great events must be transmitted uniformly is false.
This directly challenges the mutakallimun's reliance on tawatur.

If they say: If that had occurred it would have become famous, because great events must become famous, evidenced by the fact that when this event occurred in the religion of the Jews, it became famous among the people. We say: There is no dispute that these great events may become famous. As for the claim that they must become famous, this is not necessary. The proof for it is from several aspects: The first: Indeed the miracles of Muhammad, peace be upon him, such as the gushing of water from between his fingers, the feeding of a great multitude from a small amount of food, the uprooting of a tree from its root, the splitting of the moon, and the speech of the wolf, are great events [very sublime, there occurred] an impediment preventing their transmission, and yet these events were not transmitted except by one or two. So it is established that your saying that great events must be transmitted is weak. The second: Indeed the rites of the prayers were manifest and apparent for a period of twenty-three years, yet they were not transmitted as they should have been, for they differed over whether the iqama is said twice or singly, and they differed over the recitation of 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim', and they differed over the rest of the conditions.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the opponent's counter-response to the mutakallimun's previous answers. The opponent first challenges the argument about the Jewish population decrease, arguing that if it is possible for the Jews to decrease, it is possible in all types of tawatur. Then the opponent refutes the claim that great events must become widely known, using two examples from Islamic tradition: first, Muhammad's miracles (water from fingers, feeding many, uprooting tree, splitting moon, wolf speaking) were only transmitted by one or two individuals despite being great events, disproving the necessity of widespread transmission. Second, the rites of prayer were practiced openly for 23 years yet were not transmitted uniformly, as shown by differences in iqama and basmala. The passage cuts off before the third point.

Key Terms

الإقامة
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A practice performed openly for many years will be transmitted without any disagreement.
Correction: The prayer rites were performed for 23 years yet disagreements exist on details like iqama and basmala, showing that even continuous practice can have transmission gaps.

Checkpoint

A) 13 years
B) 23 years
C) 33 years
D) 43 years

Key Takeaway
The opponent's second proof shows that even a continuous, public practice like prayer can have transmission disagreements, further undermining the necessity of tawatur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have prayed thousands of times following a specific form of prayer. This lesson shows that even the Prophet's prayer was transmitted with disagreements. Are you willing to study the chains of transmission for the prayer practices you follow? Commit to one concrete step this week to learn about a single disputed practice.

The Objection That Messengers Must Be Angels
Presentation of the objection that a messenger must be an angel, with three supporting aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that a divine messenger must be an angel, and the three rational proofs offered in support of it.

Core Idea
Angels better achieve God's purpose as messengers than humans.

This lesson presents a classical objection raised against human prophets. The objectors argue that if God were to send a messenger, it would have to be an angel, and they support this with three proofs focusing on authority, trustworthiness, and honor. The author notes that this objection appears in the Quran and sets up two stations of discussion, the first being the proofs presented here.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how the objection is framed with two stations, and that only the first station is given here.
The passage ends mid-sentence at the third proof.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage gives three aspects (wujūh) supporting the claim that an angelic messenger better achieves the purpose. List them and note the reasoning behind each.
The first proof relies on fear and awe, the second on trust due to lack of worldly desires, the third on the honor of the office.
3
Reflect on the principle used
The objectors use a general principle: a wise agent always chooses the most effective means to achieve His purpose. Consider how this principle is applied here and what assumptions it makes.
This principle will be discussed further in the response (not included in this passage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني [؟سكر؟]
تقرير شبهة من يقول: أن الله تعالى لو أرسل رسولا إلى الخلق لوجب أن يكون ذلك الرسول من الملائكة
وهذه الشبهة قد ذكرها الله تعالى في القرآن مراراً وأطواراً. قالوا: الدليل عليه: أن كون الرسول من جملة الملائكة، أفضى إلى الغرض، والأفضى إلى الغرض هو الذي يفعله الفاعل الحكيم. فيفتقر ههنا إلى تقرير هذين المقامين:
المقام الأول: وهو بيان أن كون الرسول من جملة الملائكة أفضى إلى الغرض فيدل عليه وجوه:
الأول: إنه لما كان الملك في غاية القوة والقدرة والشدة، فالناس يخافونه ويهابونه، فكان انقيادهم لطاعته أكمل، فكان أفضى إلى المقصود.
والثاني: إنه إذا كان ملكاً، وكان لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا يتزوج ولا يرغب في تحصيل المال والجاه، كان وثوق الناس بصدقه أقوى، وبعدهم عن الكذب والريبة أكمل، فكان هذا الطريق أفضى إلى الغرض.
والثالث: إن منصب رسالة الله تعالى أعظم المناصب وأعزها وأشرفها،
Chapter Two [؟sakar?]
Presentation of the objection of one who says: If God Almighty sent a messenger to creation, it would be necessary that that messenger be from the angels.
And this objection has been mentioned by God Almighty in the Quran repeatedly and in various forms. They said: The proof for it is that the messenger being from the group of angels leads to the purpose, and that which leads to the purpose is what the wise agent does. So here we need to present two stations:
The first station: It is the explanation that the messenger being from the group of angels leads to the purpose, and there are aspects that indicate it:
The first: For when the angel is at the utmost strength, power, and severity, people fear him and stand in awe of him, so their submission to his obedience is more complete, thus it leads to the intended goal.
The second: For if he is an angel, and he does not eat, drink, marry, nor desire to acquire wealth and status, people's trust in his truthfulness is stronger, and their distance from lying and suspicion is more complete, so this way leads to the purpose.
The third: For the office of the message of God Almighty is the greatest, most valuable, and most honorable of offices.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents an objection raised against the necessity of human messengers. The objectors claim that if God were to send a messenger, that messenger should be an angel. This objection, the author notes, is already mentioned in the Quran. The proof offered is that an angelic messenger better achieves the divine purpose (al-gharaḍ), and a wise agent (al-fāʿil al-ḥakīm) always chooses what best achieves His purpose. The passage then sets up two stations to be discussed; the first station here is to show that an angelic messenger indeed leads to the purpose, supported by three aspects (wujūh).

First aspect: Angels possess extreme power and might, so people fear and revere them, leading to more complete obedience, thus better achieving the intended goal.

Second aspect: Angels have no human needs or desires—they do not eat, drink, marry, or seek wealth or status. Therefore, people have stronger trust in their truthfulness and are more confident in their freedom from deceit, making this path more effective for the purpose.

The third aspect is cut off at the end of the page, stating that the office of messenger is the greatest and most honorable. This likely continues to argue that an angel is more suited to such a high station.

رسالة
الملائكة
غرض
فاعل حكيم
وجوه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the objection is trivial or easily dismissed.
Correction: The objection is grounded in a rational principle (wise agent chooses best means) and has been mentioned in the Quran, showing it merits serious engagement.

Checkpoint

A) Because people are more likely to obey someone they fear and respect.
B) Because angels are more numerous than humans.

D) Because angels do not have free will.

Key Takeaway
The objectors argue that an angelic messenger is necessary because it aligns with the wisdom of a wise agent who chooses the most effective means, supported by three proofs from fear, trust, and honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Three Proofs That the Messenger Should Be an Angel
The author presents three proofs supporting that the messenger should be an angel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments presented by those who claimed that God's messenger must be an angel, and why they argue that an angelic messenger is more conducive to the purpose.

Core Idea
An angelic messenger is argued to be more effective, trustworthy, and befitting of God's honor.

This passage presents a doubt (shubhah) that is refuted in the Qur'an. The claimants offer three proofs based on effectiveness, trust, and honor. As we study these proofs, we will see the logical structure of their argument and how it relies on the principle that the wise agent does what is most conducive to the purpose.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim and principle
Read the passage to grasp the overall claim that the messenger must be an angel. Note the key principle: the wise agent does what is most conducive to the purpose.
This principle is used to argue that an angelic messenger is better.
2
Examine each proof
Look at each of the three proofs. The first focuses on fear and obedience, the second on trustworthiness, the third on honor and dignity.
Each proof is meant to show that an angelic messenger is more conducive to the purpose.
3
Consider the conclusion
The passage concludes that sending an angelic messenger is more conducive than a human one. Think about how these arguments might be refuted.
This sets up the refutation that the author will present later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني سكر تقرير شبهة من يقول: أن الله تعالى لو أرسل رسولا إلى الخلاق ليجب أن يكون ذلك الرسول من الملائكة وهذه الشبهة قد ذكرها الله تعالى في القرآن مراراً وأطواراً. قالوا: الدليل عليه: أن كون الرسول من جملة الملائكة أفضى إلى الفرض والأفضى إلى الغرض هو الذي يفعله الفاعل الحكيم. فيفتقر ههنا إلى تقرير هذين المقامين: المقام الأول: وهو بيان أن كون الرسول من جملة الملائكة أفضى إلى الغرض فيدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إنه لما كان الملك في غاية القوة والقدرة والشدة فالناس يخافونه ويهابونه فكان انقيادهم لطاعته أكمل فكان أفضى إلى المقصود. والثاني: إنه إذا كان ملكا وكان لا يأكل ولا يشرب ولا يتزوج ولا يرغب في تحصيل المال والجاه كان وثوق الناس بصدقه أقوى وبعدهم عن الكذب والريبة أكمل فكان هذا الطريق أفضى إلى الغرض. والثالث: إن منصب رسالة الله تعالى أعظم المناصب وأعزها وأشرفها والحكيم إذا فوض أعظم المناصب وأجلها إلى بعض عبيده فإنه لا يليق به إلقاء ذلك العبد في الذل والهوان ونرى أن الرسول البشري واقعاً في الذل والهوان بسبب الجوع والفقر والخوف من الأعداء والفرار من قرية إلى قرية أخرى وطلب الأموال القليلة من أصحابه. فيثبت بهذه الوجوه: إن إرسال الرسول من الملائكة أفضى إلى المقصود من إرساله من البشر.
Chapter Two: Presentation of the doubt of those who say: If God Most High sent a messenger to creation, that messenger must be from the angels. And this doubt has been mentioned by God Most High in the Qur'an repeatedly and in various ways. They said: The evidence for it is that the messenger being from the angels is more conducive to the purpose, and what is more conducive to the purpose is what the wise agent does. So we need here to establish two points: The first point: It is to explain that the messenger being from the angels is more conducive to the purpose, and there are several aspects indicating it: First: Because the angel is at the extreme of strength, power, and severity, people fear and revere him, so their obedience to him is more complete, and thus it is more conducive to the desired end. Second: Because if he is an angel, and he does not eat, drink, marry, nor desire to acquire wealth and status, people's trust in his truthfulness is stronger, and their distance from falsehood and suspicion is more complete, so this way is more conducive to the purpose. Third: Because the position of the message of God Most High is the greatest, most precious, and most honorable of positions, and if the wise one entrusts the greatest and most exalted positions to some of His servants, it is not befitting for Him to throw that servant into abasement and humiliation. And we see that the human messenger is in a state of abasement and humiliation due to hunger, poverty, fear of enemies, fleeing from one village to another, and asking for small amounts of money from his companions. So it is established by these aspects that sending the messenger from the angels is more conducive to the intended purpose than sending him from humans.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of a claim (shubhah) that God's messenger should be an angel, with three proofs. The author first states the claim and notes that it is refuted in the Qur'an. The claimants argue that the wise agent does what is most conducive to the purpose, and an angelic messenger would be more effective. Then the first point is explained with three aspects: (1) Angels inspire fear and reverence, leading to better obedience. (2) Angels are free from worldly desires, so people trust them more. (3) Human messengers suffer humiliation, which is unbefitting for the highest office. The conclusion is that an angelic messenger is more conducive to the purpose.

Misconception: That the third proof implies God is incapable of sending a human messenger.
Correction: Rather, the argument is from divine wisdom: it would be unbefitting for the wise agent to place His highest messenger in a state of humiliation.

Key Takeaway
The three proofs argue that an angelic messenger is more effective (through fear), more trustworthy (free from worldly desires), and more honorable (not subject to humiliation) than a human messenger.

Three Objections to an Angelic Messenger and Answer to the First
The author lists three objections to an angelic messenger and refutes the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three objections raised against the idea of an angelic messenger and how the first objection is refuted by appealing to divine power and miracle.

Core Idea
Fear of an angel can be overcome by divine intervention, making it a miracle.

In debates about prophethood, opponents argue that a messenger must be human. Here, the author presents three arguments against sending an angel as a messenger, then addresses the first: that seeing an angel in original form causes fear. He shows that God can remove that fear, turning it into a sign of truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read its literal translation. Notice the structure: objections numbered with 'first', 'second', 'third', followed by 'we said' for the answer.
The text cuts off mid-sentence; we only have the answer to the first objection.
2
Identify the three objections
List the three objections: (1) seeing an angel in original form causes fear and loss of reason; in borrowed form there is no difference from human. (2) Angels are severe and harsh, unlike humans. (3) Like inclines to like; humans prefer a messenger from their own kind.
3
Analyze the refutation of the first objection
The author argues that since God creates fear, He can also create courage in human hearts so that they do not panic when seeing an angel. This miraculous absence of fear becomes evidence for the angel's truthfulness.
Notice how the author turns the potential obstacle into a positive sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: إرسال الرسول من الملائكة يوجب أنواعاً من المفاسد أولها: أن الأمة إما أن يشاهدوا ذلك الملك على صورته الأصلية أو على صورة أخرى مستعارة والأول يوجب الخوف الشديد وزوال العقل ألا ترى أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما رأى جبريل عليه السلام على خلقته الأصلية غشى عليه والثاني باطل لأنه إذا رأى الملك على صورة الإنسان فحينئذ لا يبقى بينه وبين الإنسان فرق. وثانيها: إن الملائكة فيهم شدة عظيمة وقهر شديد فهم لا يسامحون البشر في زلاتهم ومعاصيهم بخلاف الرسول البشري. وثالثها: إن الجنس إلى الجنس أميل فإلف الناس برسول يأتيهم من جنسهم أكمل من الفهم بالملك. قلنا: أما السؤال الأول فمدفوع فإنا نقول: خلق الخوف والفزع في قلوب العباد من الله تعالى فكان يجب أن يجعل قلوب البشر بحيث إذا الملك لم يفزعوا منه فيصير هذا المعنى معجزة على صدق ذلك الملك
For they say: Sending the messenger from the angels entails categories of corruption. First: The community either sees that angel in his original form or in another borrowed form. The first causes intense fear and loss of reason—do you not see that when the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, saw Gabriel, peace be upon him, in his original form, he fainted? And the second is invalid because if he sees the angel in human form, then there is no difference between him and a human. Second: Angels have great severity and harsh domination, so they do not tolerate humans in their slips and sins, unlike a human messenger. Third: Like inclines to like, so people's familiarity with a messenger from their own kind is more complete than their understanding with an angel. We said: As for the first question, it is rebutted. For we say: The creation of fear and panic in the hearts of servants is from God Most High. So He should make the hearts of humans such that when they see the angel, they do not panic, and this meaning becomes a miracle attesting to the truthfulness of that angel.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents three objections against the claim that the messenger should be an angel, followed by the author's refutation of the first objection. The three objections are: (1) Seeing an angel in his original form causes extreme fear and loss of reason, while seeing him in human form eliminates any distinction. (2) Angels are severe and harsh, so they would not be lenient with human shortcomings. (3) Humans naturally gravitate towards their own kind, so a human messenger is more relatable. The author responds to the first objection by arguing that since God creates fear in hearts, He could also create courage in human hearts so that they do not panic when seeing an angel, and this would serve as a miracle confirming the angel's truthfulness. The second and third objections are left unanswered in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection about fear is logically unanswerable because seeing an angel naturally causes terror.
Correction: The author shows that God, who creates fear, can also prevent it, making the absence of fear a miraculous sign of the angel's truthfulness.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Sending an Angel: A Proof from Wisdom
Author argues that sending an angelic messenger is more befitting to God's wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that God's wisdom requires sending an angelic messenger rather than a human one.

Core Idea
A wise God would not entrust the highest mission to someone He allows to be humiliated.

This short passage presents a theological proof based on divine wisdom. The author contends that if God appoints a human messenger, that messenger's worldly hardships—hunger, poverty, fear—would contradict God's wisdom. Therefore, an angelic messenger is more befitting. Let's examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's flow come through.
Notice the tight logical structure: premise, observation, conclusion.
2
Identify the premise about wisdom
The author starts with a general rule: a wise person does not humiliate someone to whom he entrusts a great position. Understand why this is considered self-evident.
This premise is key to the argument.
3
Observe the description of the human messenger
The author lists specific hardships: hunger, poverty, fear, fleeing, begging. See how these are examples of 'humiliation and lowliness'.
Think about whether these are necessarily humiliating.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that since human messengers suffer these, and God is wise, He would not send a human; rather, an angel is more conducive to the purpose.
The conclusion is stated as 'established by these considerations'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكيم إذا فوض أعظم المناصب وأجلها إلى بعض عبيده، فإنه لا يليق به إلقاء ذلك العبد في الذل والهوان. ونرى أن الرسول البشري واقعاً في الذل والهوان، بسبب الجوع والفقر والخوف من الأعداء والفرار من قرية إلى قرية أخرى، وطلب الأموال القليلة من أصحابه. فيثبت بهذه الوجوه: إن إرسال الرسول من الملائكة أفضى إلى المقصود من إرساله من البشر.
The wise one, when he delegates the greatest and most eminent positions to some of his servants, it is not befitting for him to cast that servant into humiliation and lowliness. And we see that the human messenger is [actually] in humiliation and lowliness, due to hunger, poverty, fear of enemies, fleeing from one village to another, and asking for small amounts of money from his companions. So it is established by these considerations that sending the messenger from the angels is more conducive to the purpose than sending him from humans.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from divine wisdom. The author argues that if God, in His wisdom, entrusts the greatest positions (prophethood) to some servants, it would contradict His wisdom to then allow that servant to suffer humiliation. Yet we observe that human messengers experience humiliation through hunger, poverty, fear, flight, and begging for small sums. Therefore, since God is wise, He would not choose a human for the exalted role of messenger if it leads to such humiliation. Thus, sending an angelic messenger, who is free from these worldly needs, is more fitting and more conducive to achieving the purpose of prophethood. The author concludes that the evidence shows that sending a messenger from the angels better accomplishes the intended objective than sending one from humans.

Key Terms
رسول
ملائكة
حكيم
ذل وهوان
مقصود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the prophet's worldly hardships disprove his prophethood, or that they are signs of divine anger.
Correction: The author uses these hardships not to deny prophethood, but to argue that a human messenger is inappropriate; thus the true messenger must be an angel.

Checkpoint

A) Great power and wealth
B) Humiliation and lowliness
C) Perfect knowledge
D) Angelic nature

Key Takeaway
The wisdom of God requires that the greatest mission be entrusted to an angelic messenger, not a human subject to humiliation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When I see God's chosen servants—whether prophets or righteous people—suffering, do I ever question God's wisdom or their status? How does this lesson challenge me to trust that God's ways are perfect even when they involve hardship?
?
The author says it is unbefitting for a wise person to humiliate a high-ranking servant. In my own life, do I ever treat those under my authority with disrespect or humiliation? Am I willing to examine my actions and repent?
?
If I were given a great responsibility, would I expect comfort and honor? How does the reality that human messengers faced hunger, poverty, and fear teach me about true dignity, and what change must I make in my perspective on worldly success?

Refutation of the First Objection: Fear and Distinction
First objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that seeing an angel in original form causes fear and that appearing in human form removes distinction.

Core Idea
God can remove fear and distinguish an angel without causing terror.

The first objection claims that an angelic messenger would either terrify people in original form or be indistinguishable in human form. The author responds by pointing out that God can create hearts fearless of the angel, making it a miracle, and that the angel can appear human but be distinguished by not needing food, drink, clothing, or marriage. Let's see how he builds this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the first objection
Carefully read the first objection, which presents two options: seeing the angel in original form causes fear and loss of reason; seeing him in borrowed human form leaves no difference from ordinary humans.
The example of the Prophet fainting when seeing Gabriel is given.
2
Examine the refutation: removing fear
Notice that the author first refutes by saying God could have made people fearless, turning the absence of fear into a miracle.
3
Examine the refutation: distinction without fear
Then he argues that the angel can appear in human form but be distinguished by not needing basic human necessities, which is enough to differentiate without causing intense fear.
Compare this to a human prophet who also has human needs.
4
Reflect on the overall logic
Consider how the refutation directly addresses each part of the objection: the fear issue and the distinction issue.
This shows a methodical response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: إرسال الرسول من الملائكة، يوجب أنواعاً من المفاسد. أولها: أن الأمة إما أن يشاهدوا ذلك الملك على صورته الأصلية، أو على صورة أخرى مستعارة، والأول يوجب الخوف الشديد، وزوال العقل. ألا ترى أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما رأى جبريل عليه السلام على خلقته الأصلية غشى عليه. والثاني باطل. لأنه إذا رأى الملك على صورة الإنسان، فحينئذ لا يبقى بينه وبين الإنسان فرق. وثانيها: إن الملائكة فيهم شدة عظيمة وقهر شديد، فهم لا يسامحون البشر في زلاتهم ومعاصيهم، بخلاف الرسول البشري. وثالثها: إن الجنس إلى الجنس أميل. فإلف الناس برسول يأتيهم من جنسهم، أكمل من الفهم بالملك. قلنا: أما السؤال الأول فمدفوع. فإنا نقول: خلق الخوف والفزع في قلوب العباد من الله تعالى، فكان يجب أن يجعل قلوب البشر بحيث إذا شاهدوا الملك لم يفزعوا منه، فيصير هذا المعنى معجزة على صدق ذلك الملك. ثم نقول: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن الناس يشاهدون ذلك الملك في صورة البشر؟ ويكون الفرق بينه وبين سائر البشر: أن لا يحتاج إلى الأكل والشرب والملبوس والمنكوح، وهذا القدر من التفاوت لا يوجب الخوف الشديد، ويحصل الامتياز بينه وبين سائر الناس. وأما قوله ثانيا: الملائكة لهم قهر شديد فهم لا يسامحون البشر. قلنا: الملائكة لا يعصون الله فيما يأمرهم، فإذا أمرهم بالرفق لم يفعلوا شيئاً من التشديد. وأما قوله ثالثاً: الجنس إلى الجنس أميل. فنقول: حصول الميل في القلب، ليس إلا من الله تعالى، كما قال تعالى: ( ولكن الله ألف بينهم ) فيثبت بما ذكرنا: أن إرسال الرسول من زمرة الملائكة، أفضى إلى المقصود. ونقول: لو كانت الرسالة جائزة، لوجب أن يكون ذلك الرسول من الملائكة، لأن الحكيم إذا أراد تحصيل مطلوب، وكان له إليه طريقان، وكان أحد الطريقين أفضى إلى حصول ذلك المطلوب من الطريق الثاني، فإنه يجب عليه بمقتضى حكمته، أن يرجح الطريق الأفضل الأكمل.
For if they say: Sending a messenger from the angels entails types of evils. First: The community either sees that angel in his original form or in another borrowed form. The first causes severe fear and loss of reason. Do you not see that when the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) saw Gabriel (peace be upon him) in his original form, he fainted? The second is invalid, because if the angel is seen in human form, then there is no difference between him and a human. Second: The angels have great severity and intense overpowering, so they do not pardon humans for their slips and sins, unlike the human messenger. Third: Likeness is more inclined to likeness. Therefore, people's familiarity with a messenger who comes from their own kind is more complete than understanding through an angel. We say: As for the first objection, it is refuted. For we say: God Almighty created fear and terror in the hearts of servants, so He should have made the hearts of humans such that when they see the angel they would not be terrified, and this would become a miracle attesting to the truthfulness of that angel. Then we say: Why is it not permissible to say that people see that angel in human form? And the difference between him and other humans is that he has no need for eating, drinking, clothing, and marriage. This amount of differentiation does not cause intense fear, and distinction between him and other people is achieved. As for his second statement: Angels have intense overpowering, so they do not pardon humans. We say: Angels do not disobey God in what He commands them; if He commands them to be gentle, they do nothing of harshness. As for his third statement: Likeness is more inclined to likeness. We say: The occurrence of inclination in the heart is only from God Almighty, as He said: 'But God brought affection between them.' So it is established by what we have mentioned that sending the messenger from the company of angels is more conducive to the purpose. And we say: If messengership were permissible, it would be necessary that the messenger be from the angels, because the Wise One, when He wants to attain a desired objective and has two ways to it, and one of the two ways is more conducive to attaining that objective than the second, then it is incumbent upon Him, by virtue of His wisdom, to prefer the better and more complete way.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents three objections against sending an angelic messenger and the author's refutations. The first objection: seeing an angel in his original form causes terror and loss of reason, as happened to the Prophet when he saw Gabriel; but if the angel appears in borrowed human form, there is no distinction from ordinary humans. The author answers: God could make the people's hearts fearless of the angel, making it a miracle; also, the angel can appear in human form but be distinguished by not needing food, drink, clothing, or marriage—sufficient to differentiate without causing fear. Second objection: angels are severe and do not tolerate human sins, unlike a human messenger. Answer: Angels obey God; if God commands gentleness, they are gentle. Third objection: people are more attracted to their own kind. Answer: Inclination comes from God, as the Quran says, so God can create affection for an angelic messenger. After refuting, the author reiterates that sending an angel is more conducive to the purpose, and adds a further argument from divine wisdom: if there are two paths to a goal, the wiser is to choose the better path; since an angelic messenger is better, God would choose him.

Key Terms
صورة أصلية
صورة مستعارة
خوف
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels cannot appear in human form without causing confusion or fear.
Correction: They can appear in human form with clear distinguishing traits (no needs) and God can remove fear, making it a miracle.

Checkpoint
How does the author propose to distinguish an angel appearing in human form from an ordinary human?
A) By his radiant light
B) By his lack of need for food, drink, clothing, and marriage
C) By his wings
D) By his ability to perform miracles

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the first objection by arguing that God can prevent fear and that an angel can be distinguished by not needing human necessities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you let fear of something unfamiliar or overwhelming prevent you from accepting a truth or a sign from God? How does this lesson's claim that God can remove fear challenge you to reconsider those moments?
?
The objector argues that an angel in human form is indistinguishable, but the author says distinction lies in not needing necessities. In your life, what subtle but real signs from God or His guidance might you be overlooking because you expect dramatic, unmistakable signs?
?
If God removed fear from your heart right now, what would you be willing to do or believe that you currently avoid? What step can you take this week to act on that possibility?

Refutation of the Second Objection: Angelic Severity
Second objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that angels are too severe and unforgiving to be messengers to humans.

Core Idea
Angels obey God completely; if God commands gentleness, they are gentle.

The second objection claims that angels are inherently harsh and do not pardon human mistakes, unlike a human messenger. The author counters by emphasizing that angels are fully obedient to God: if God commands them to be gentle, they will be gentle. This lesson examines that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection
Read the objection: angels have great severity and do not pardon humans for their slips, unlike a human messenger.
This is a common perception of angels as stern.
2
Examine the refutation
Notice the author's response: angels do not disobey God; if God commands them to be gentle, they act gently.
The refutation relies on the absolute obedience of angels.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this refutation shows that the severity of angels is not an obstacle if God wills otherwise.
God's command overrides any inherent nature.

According to the author, what prevents angels from being harsh when sent as messengers?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone’s suitability for a task based on a perceived fixed flaw, only to realize that flaw could be transformed by obedience to a higher command? ?
If angels, who are far more powerful than you, submit completely to God’s command without hesitation, what does your own resistance to a particular divine command reveal about your heart? This lesson shows that obedience can reshape character. Which command of God do you find hardest to obey because you think it doesn't fit your personality? Will you surrender that excuse to God today?

Refutation of the Third Objection: Inclination to One's Kind
Third objection and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that people are more inclined to messengers of their own kind by arguing that inclination comes from God.

Core Idea
Inclination in hearts is created by God, not by natural similarity alone.

The third objection asserts that people naturally feel more familiarity and affection for a messenger from their own species. The author counters by citing the Quranic principle that God Himself creates affection between hearts. This lesson unpacks that refutation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the third objection
Read the objection: likeness is more inclined to likeness, so people are more familiar with a human messenger than an angel.
This is based on a psychological observation.
2
Examine the refutation
Notice the author's response: inclination in the heart is only from God, quoting Quran 8:63
The verse is 'But God brought affection between them.'
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that sending an angel is more conducive to the purpose, as God can create affection for the angel.
This refutation undermines the basis of the objection.

What Quranic verse does the author cite to support his refutation?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a deep connection to someone because they share your background or beliefs, do you recognize that God is the one who placed that affection in your heart? How would your relationship change if you consistently attributed that bond to His will rather than to natural similarity?
?
If God can create affection for an angelic messenger—a being not of your kind—what does that say about your excuses for not loving certain people or embracing difficult truths? Are you limiting God's power by assuming your heart cannot be changed?
?
The objection in this lesson assumes that natural similarity is necessary for acceptance. What 'natural' barriers do you assume are insurmountable in your own life? Will you ask God today to break that assumption and create in you a new inclination?

The Wisdom of Sending an Angelic Messenger
Concluding wisdom argument for angelic messenger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's final argument that divine wisdom requires preferring the better path, and thus an angelic messenger is more fitting.

Core Idea
If two paths exist, the wiser must choose the better one; an angel is better.

After refuting the three objections, the author adds a positive argument from divine wisdom: if there are two ways to achieve a goal, the Wise One must choose the better way. Since an angelic messenger is more perfect than a human one, it would be necessary for God to send an angel. This lesson lays out that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the wisdom argument
Read the passage: if messengership were permissible, the messenger must be from angels because the Wise One chooses the better of two ways.
This is a separate, positive argument.
2
Understand the premise
The author assumes that an angelic messenger is more perfect and effective than a human one.
This builds on the earlier refutations.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
God's wisdom necessitates preferring the better path, so an angel must be sent.
This argument reinforces the overall thesis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: إرسال الرسول من الملائكة، يوجب أنواعاً من المفاسد. أولها: أن الأمة إما أن يشاهدوا ذلك الملك على صورته الأصلية، أو على صورة أخرى مستعارة، والأول يوجب الخوف الشديد، وزوال العقل. ألا ترى أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما رأى جبريل عليه السلام على خلقته الأصلية غشى عليه. والثاني باطل. لأنه إذا رأى الملك على صورة الإنسان، فحينئذ لا يبقى بينه وبين الإنسان فرق. وثانيها: إن الملائكة فيهم شدة عظيمة وقهر شديد، فهم لا يسامحون البشر في زلاتهم ومعاصيهم، بخلاف الرسول البشري. وثالثها: إن الجنس إلى الجنس أميل. فإلف الناس برسول يأتيهم من جنسهم، أكمل من الفهم بالملك. قلنا: أما السؤال الأول فمدفوع. فإنا نقول: خلق الخوف والفزع في قلوب العباد من الله تعالى، فكان يجب أن يجعل قلوب البشر بحيث إذا شاهدوا الملك لم يفزعوا منه، فيصير هذا المعنى معجزة على صدق ذلك الملك. ثم نقول: لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن الناس يشاهدون ذلك الملك في صورة البشر؟ ويكون الفرق بينه وبين سائر البشر: أن لا يحتاج إلى الأكل والشرب والملبوس والمنكوح، وهذا القدر من التفاوت لا يوجب الخوف الشديد، ويحصل الامتياز بينه وبين سائر الناس. وأما قوله ثانيا: الملائكة لهم قهر شديد فهم لا يسامحون البشر. قلنا: الملائكة لا يعصون الله فيما يأمرهم، فإذا أمرهم بالرفق لم يفعلوا شيئاً من التشديد. وأما قوله ثالثاً: الجنس إلى الجنس أميل. فنقول: حصول الميل في القلب، ليس إلا من الله تعالى، كما قال تعالى: ( ولكن الله ألف بينهم ) فيثبت بما ذكرنا: أن إرسال الرسول من زمرة الملائكة، أفضى إلى المقصود. ونقول: لو كانت الرسالة جائزة، لوجب أن يكون ذلك الرسول من الملائكة، لأن الحكيم إذا أراد تحصيل مطلوب، وكان له إليه طريقان، وكان أحد الطريقين أفضى إلى حصول ذلك المطلوب من الطريق الثاني، فإنه يجب عليه بمقتضى حكمته، أن يرجح الطريق الأفضل الأكمل.
For if they say: Sending a messenger from the angels entails types of evils. First: The community either sees that angel in his original form or in another borrowed form. The first causes severe fear and loss of reason. Do you not see that when the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) saw Gabriel (peace be upon him) in his original form, he fainted? The second is invalid, because if the angel is seen in human form, then there is no difference between him and a human. Second: The angels have great severity and intense overpowering, so they do not pardon humans for their slips and sins, unlike the human messenger. Third: Likeness is more inclined to likeness. Therefore, people's familiarity with a messenger who comes from their own kind is more complete than understanding through an angel. We say: As for the first objection, it is refuted. For we say: God Almighty created fear and terror in the hearts of servants, so He should have made the hearts of humans such that when they see the angel they would not be terrified, and this would become a miracle attesting to the truthfulness of that angel. Then we say: Why is it not permissible to say that people see that angel in human form? And the difference between him and other humans is that he has no need for eating, drinking, clothing, and marriage. This amount of differentiation does not cause intense fear, and distinction between him and other people is achieved. As for his second statement: Angels have intense overpowering, so they do not pardon humans. We say: Angels do not disobey God in what He commands them; if He commands them to be gentle, they do nothing of harshness. As for his third statement: Likeness is more inclined to likeness. We say: The occurrence of inclination in the heart is only from God Almighty, as He said: 'But God brought affection between them.' So it is established by what we have mentioned that sending the messenger from the company of angels is more conducive to the purpose. And we say: If messengership were permissible, it would be necessary that the messenger be from the angels, because the Wise One, when He wants to attain a desired objective and has two ways to it, and one of the two ways is more conducive to attaining that objective than the second, then it is incumbent upon Him, by virtue of His wisdom, to prefer the better and more complete way.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents three objections against sending an angelic messenger and the author's refutations. The first objection: seeing an angel in his original form causes terror and loss of reason, as happened to the Prophet when he saw Gabriel; but if the angel appears in borrowed human form, there is no distinction from ordinary humans. The author answers: God could make the people's hearts fearless of the angel, making it a miracle; also, the angel can appear in human form but be distinguished by not needing food, drink, clothing, or marriage—sufficient to differentiate without causing fear. Second objection: angels are severe and do not tolerate human sins, unlike a human messenger. Answer: Angels obey God; if God commands gentleness, they are gentle. Third objection: people are more attracted to their own kind. Answer: Inclination comes from God, as the Quran says, so God can create affection for an angelic messenger. After refuting, the author reiterates that sending an angel is more conducive to the purpose, and adds a further argument from divine wisdom: if there are two paths to a goal, the wiser is to choose the better path; since an angelic messenger is better, God would choose him.

Key Terms
حكيم
مقصود
طريق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why must the messenger be from the angels?
A) Because angels are more numerous
B) Because they are more obedient
C) Because wisdom requires choosing the better path
D) Because humans are sinful

Key Takeaway
Divine wisdom necessitates sending an angelic messenger, as it is the better path.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a choice between two options, do you honestly choose the better one, or do you settle for what is easier? What does that reveal about how much you trust God's wisdom in your life?
?
If you truly believed that God always chooses the best for you (even when it's difficult), would you change any decision you are currently avoiding? What is holding you back?
?
The passage says God's wisdom obliges Him to choose the better path. Is your life evidence that you believe God has chosen the best path for you, or do you resent His choices? Ask yourself: do I secretly wish God had chosen differently for me?

The Case for Angelic Messengers: Perfection and Freedom from Deficiency
Author argues that angels are more perfect and thus more suitable as messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument that angels are more suitable as messengers due to their perfection and freedom from human deficiencies.

Core Idea
Only a perfect being free from deficiency can perfect others without infinite regress.

This passage presents a second philosophical argument for why angels are better suited to convey divine messages than humans. It builds on the idea that perfection requires freedom from the defects inherent in human nature, such as lust and anger. The argument uses the impossibility of infinite regress to show that the perfecter must be free from deficiency, and only angels meet this condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the overall logic: definition of human perfection, observation of deficiency, need for a perfecter, requirement of freedom from deficiency (otherwise regress), human defects, angelic purity, conclusion.
Pay attention to the word 'تسلسل' (infinite regress) – a key concept in Islamic theology.
2
Identify the key concepts
Find definitions of 'كمال' (perfection) and 'نقصان' (deficiency) in the passage. Also locate 'مكمل' (perfecter) and 'تسلسل' (infinite regress).
The perfecter is called 'المكمل' – the one who makes others perfect.
3
Analyze the logical structure
The argument follows a conditional: if the perfecter were deficient, he would need another perfecter → infinite regress. Therefore, the perfecter must be free from deficiency. Understand why this regress is unacceptable in Islamic thought.
Infinite regress is impossible because it would mean no ultimate perfecter.
4
Apply to the angel vs. human debate
The passage concludes that angels are more appropriate because they are free from lust/anger and absorbed in divine knowledge. Contrast this with humans who inherently have these deficiencies.
The author assumes that a messenger must be a perfecter of others, a key premise.
5
Reflect on underlying assumptions
Ask yourself: Is it necessary that a prophet/messenger be a perfecter of others? This argument is part of a larger objection; understanding its premises helps evaluate its strength.
The lesson does not require you to accept or reject the argument, but to understand it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في تقرير هذه الشبهة: إن كمال الإنسان في أن يعرف الحق لذاته، والخير لأجل العمل به. ونرى البشر ناقصين في هذين الوصفين، فاحتاجوا إلى شخص يكون كاملاً فيهما، حتى يصير ذلك الكامل مكملا للناقصين، وذلك المكمل يجب أن يكون مبرا عن النقصان في هذين الوصفين، وإلا لافتقر إلى مكمل آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وكل من كان بشراً فإنه لا ينفك عن الشهوة والغضب، وبسبب حصول هذين الوصفين يكون النقصان. أما الملائكة فهم مقدسون عن الشهوة والغضب، والخيال والوهم حاصل فيهم، مستغرقون في المعارف الإلهية مواظبون على الطاعات والعبادات، فكانت بعثتهم لأجل تكميل الناقصين أولى.
The second aspect of expounding this objection: Human perfection consists in knowing truth for its own sake and good for the sake of acting upon it. And we see that humans are deficient in these two attributes, so they need a person who is perfect in them, so that that perfect one may perfect the deficient ones. And that perfecter must be free from deficiency in these two attributes; otherwise he would need another perfecter, and an infinite regress would follow. And every human is never free from lust and anger, and due to the presence of these two attributes, deficiency occurs. As for the angels, they are purified from lust and anger, and imagination and caprice are present in them [?], they are absorbed in divine cognitions, constant in acts of obedience and worship. So sending them for the sake of perfecting the deficient ones is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument for why angels are better messengers. The author states that human perfection lies in knowing truth for its own sake and doing good for the sake of action. Humans are deficient in both, so they need a perfect being to guide them. That perfect being must be free from deficiency, otherwise he would need yet another perfecter, leading to an infinite regress. But every human has lust and anger, which cause deficiency. Angels, however, are free from lust and anger, absorbed in divine knowledge, and constant in worship. Therefore, sending angels to perfect deficient humans is more fitting and avoids regress.

Key Terms
كمال
نقصان
شهوة وغضب
تسلسل
مبرا
مكمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A human prophet can be so spiritually advanced that he overcomes lust and anger, making him perfect and thus a suitable perfecter.
Correction: The argument holds that lust and anger are inherent to human nature and cannot be completely shed; any human with these attributes is deficient and would require another perfecter, leading to infinite regress.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider angels more suitable than humans as perfecters of others?
A) Angels are stronger
B) Angels are free from lust and anger and absorbed in divine knowledge
C) Angels can fly
D) Angels are immortal

Key Takeaway
Angels are more suitable than humans as messengers because they are free from the deficiencies inherent in human nature, which would otherwise lead to an infinite regress of perfecters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where in your life do you still allow your شهوة (lust) and غضب (anger) to prevent you from knowing truth and doing good? What will you do today to seek purification from these deficiencies?
?
This lesson teaches that only a perfect being can perfect others. Have you been relying on flawed human guidance without turning to the ultimate source of perfection—Allah and His revelation? How will you change your priorities starting now?
?
Angels are described as 'مستغرقون في المعارف الإلهية' (absorbed in divine knowledge). What worldly distraction absorbs you most and pulls you away from seeking divine knowledge? What concrete step will you take this week to become more absorbed in knowing Allah?
